         <div class="postcell post-layout--right">
          <div class="s-prose js-post-body" itemprop="text">
           <p>
            I have an object:
           </p>
           <pre><code>myObject = { 'a': 1, 'b': 2, 'c': 3 }
</code></pre>
           <p>
            I am looking for a native method, similar to
            <code>
             Array.prototype.map
            </code>
            that would be used as follows:
           </p>
           <pre><code>newObject = myObject.map(function (value, label) {
    return value * value;
});

// newObject is now { 'a': 1, 'b': 4, 'c': 9 }
</code></pre>
           <p>
            Does JavaScript have such a
            <code>
             map
            </code>
            function for objects? (I want this for Node.JS, so I don't care about cross-browser issues.)
           </p>
          </div>
          <div class="mt24 mb12">
           <div class="post-taglist d-flex gs4 gsy fd-column">
            <div class="d-flex ps-relative fw-wrap">
             <a class="post-tag" href="/questions/tagged/javascript" rel="tag" title="show questions tagged 'javascript'">

             </a>

             </a>

                </code>

        <a name="14810722">
        </a>
        <div class="answer js-answer accepted-answer" data-answerid="14810722" data-highest-scored="1" data-position-on-page="1" data-question-has-accepted-highest-score="1" data-score="2169" id="answer-14810722" itemprop="acceptedAnswer" itemscope="" itemtype="https://schema.org/Answer">
         <div class="post-layout">
          <div class="votecell post-layout--left">
           <div class="js-voting-container d-flex jc-center fd-column ai-stretch gs4 fc-black-200" data-post-id="14810722">
            <button aria-label="Up vote" aria-pressed="false" class="js-vote-up-btn flex--item s-btn s-btn__unset c-pointer" data-controller="s-tooltip" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" data-selected-classes="fc-theme-primary" data-unselected-classes="" title="This answer is useful">
             <svg aria-hidden="true" class="svg-icon iconArrowUpLg" height="36" viewbox="0 0 36 36" width="36">
              <path d="M2 25h32L18 9 2 25Z">
              </path>
             </svg>
            </button>
            <div class="js-vote-count flex--item d-flex fd-column ai-center fc-black-500 fs-title" data-value="2169" itemprop="upvoteCount">
             2169
            </div>
            <button aria-label="Down vote" aria-pressed="false" class="js-vote-down-btn flex--item s-btn s-btn__unset c-pointer" data-controller="s-tooltip" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" data-selected-classes="fc-theme-primary" data-unselected-classes="" title="This answer is not useful">
             <svg aria-hidden="true" class="svg-icon iconArrowDownLg" height="36" viewbox="0 0 36 36" width="36">
              <path d="M2 11h32L18 27 2 11Z">
              </path>
             </svg>
            </button>
            <div aria-label="Accepted" class="js-accepted-answer-indicator flex--item fc-green-500 py6 mtn8" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" role="note" tabindex="0" title="Loading when this answer was accepted…">
             <div class="ta-center">
              <svg aria-hidden="true" class="svg-icon iconCheckmarkLg" height="36" viewbox="0 0 36 36" width="36">
               <path d="m6 14 8 8L30 6v8L14 30l-8-8v-8Z">
               </path>
              </svg>
             </div>
            </div>
            <a aria-label="Timeline" class="js-post-issue flex--item s-btn s-btn__unset c-pointer py6 mx-auto" data-controller="s-tooltip" data-ks-title="timeline" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" data-shortcut="T" href="/posts/14810722/timeline" title="Show activity on this post.">
             <svg aria-hidden="true" class="mln2 mr0 svg-icon iconHistory" height="18" viewbox="0 0 19 18" width="19">
              <path d="M3 9a8 8 0 1 1 3.73 6.77L8.2 14.3A6 6 0 1 0 5 9l3.01-.01-4 4-4-4h3L3 9Zm7-4h1.01L11 9.36l3.22 2.1-.6.93L10 10V5Z">
              </path>
             </svg>
            </a>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="answercell post-layout--right">
           <div class="s-prose js-post-body" itemprop="text">
            <p>
             There is no native
             <code>
              map
             </code>
             to the
             <code>
              Object
             </code>
             object, but how about this:
            </p>
            <p>
             <div class="snippet" data-babel="false" data-console="true" data-hide="false" data-lang="js">
              <div class="snippet-code">
               <pre class="snippet-code-js lang-js prettyprint-override"><code>var myObject = { 'a': 1, 'b': 2, 'c': 3 };

Object.keys(myObject).map(function(key, index) {
  myObject[key] *= 2;
});

console.log(myObject);
// =&gt; { 'a': 2, 'b': 4, 'c': 6 }</code></pre>
              </div>
             </div>
            </p>
            <p>
             But you could easily iterate over an object using
             <code>
              for ... in
             </code>
             :
            </p>
            <p>
             <div class="snippet" data-babel="false" data-console="true" data-hide="false" data-lang="js">
              <div class="snippet-code">
               <pre class="snippet-code-js lang-js prettyprint-override"><code>var myObject = { 'a': 1, 'b': 2, 'c': 3 };

for (var key in myObject) {
  if (myObject.hasOwnProperty(key)) {
    myObject[key] *= 2;
  }
}

console.log(myObject);
// { 'a': 2, 'b': 4, 'c': 6 }</code></pre>
              </div>
             </div>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Update
             </strong>
            </p>
            <p>
             A lot of people are mentioning that the previous methods do not return a new object, but rather operate on the object itself. For that matter I wanted to add another solution that returns a new object and leaves the original object as it is:
            </p>
            <p>
             <div class="snippet" data-babel="false" data-console="true" data-hide="false" data-lang="js">
              <div class="snippet-code">
               <pre class="snippet-code-js lang-js prettyprint-override"><code>var myObject = { 'a': 1, 'b': 2, 'c': 3 };

// returns a new object with the values at each key mapped using mapFn(value)
function objectMap(object, mapFn) {
  return Object.keys(object).reduce(function(result, key) {
    result[key] = mapFn(object[key])
    return result
  }, {})
}

var newObject = objectMap(myObject, function(value) {
  return value * 2
})

console.log(newObject);
// =&gt; { 'a': 2, 'b': 4, 'c': 6 }

console.log(myObject);
// =&gt; { 'a': 1, 'b': 2, 'c': 3 }</code></pre>
              </div>
             </div>
            </p>
            <p>
             <a href="https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/JavaScript/Reference/Global_Objects/Array/Reduce" rel="noreferrer">
              <code>
               Array.prototype.reduce
              </code>
             </a>
             reduces an array to a single value by somewhat merging the previous value with the current. The chain is initialized by an empty object
             <code>
              {}
             </code>
             . On every iteration a new key of
             <code>
              myObject
             </code>
             is added with twice the key as the value.
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Update
             </strong>
            </p>
            <p>
             With new ES6 features, there is a more elegant way to express
             <code>
              objectMap
             </code>
             .
            </p>
            <p>
             <div class="snippet" data-babel="false" data-console="true" data-hide="false" data-lang="js">
              <div class="snippet-code">
               <pre class="snippet-code-js lang-js prettyprint-override"><code>const objectMap = (obj, fn) =&gt;
  Object.fromEntries(
    Object.entries(obj).map(
      ([k, v], i) =&gt; [k, fn(v, k, i)]
    )
  )
  
const myObject = { a: 1, b: 2, c: 3 }

console.log(objectMap(myObject, v =&gt; 2 * v)) </code></pre>
              </div>
             </div>
            </p>
           </div>
           <div class="mt24">
            <div class="d-flex fw-wrap ai-start jc-end gs8 gsy">
             <time datetime="2013-02-11T10:52:37" itemprop="dateCreated">
             </time>
             <div class="flex--item mr16" style="flex: 1 1 100px;">
              <div class="js-post-menu pt2" data-post-id="14810722">

                <span class="comment-copy">
                 @KhalilRavanna I think you've misread the code here - this answer isn't using
                 <code>
                  map
                 </code>
                 correctly because it isn't doing a
                 <code>
                  return
                 </code>
                 - it's abusing
                 <code>
                  map
                 </code>
                 as if it were a
                 <code>
                  forEach
                 </code>
                 call.  If he actually
                 <i>
                  did
                 </i>
                 <code>
                  return myObject[value] * 2
                 </code>
                 then the result would be an
                 <i>
                  array
                 </i>
                 containing the original values doubled, instead of an
                 <i>
                  object
                 </i>
                 containing the original keys with doubled values, the latter clearly being what the OP asked for.
                </span>

                <span class="comment-copy">
                 @Amberlamps your
                 <code>
                  .reduce
                 </code>
                 example is OK, but IMHO it still falls a long way short of the convenience of a
                 <code>
                  .map
                 </code>
                 for Objects, since your
                 <code>
                  .reduce
                 </code>
                 callback not only has to match the way that
                 <code>
                  .reduce
                 </code>
                 works, but also requires that
                 <code>
                  myObject
                 </code>
                 be available in the lexical scope.  The latter in particular makes it impossible to just pass a function reference in the callback, requiring an in-place anonymous function instead.
                </span>
                <div class="d-inline-flex ai-center">

                 </code>
                 instead.

        </a>
        <div class="answer js-answer" data-answerid="38829074" data-highest-scored="0" data-position-on-page="2" data-question-has-accepted-highest-score="1" data-score="462" id="answer-38829074" itemprop="suggestedAnswer" itemscope="" itemtype="https://schema.org/Answer">
         <div class="post-layout">
          <div class="votecell post-layout--left">
           <div class="js-voting-container d-flex jc-center fd-column ai-stretch gs4 fc-black-200" data-post-id="38829074">
            <button aria-label="Up vote" aria-pressed="false" class="js-vote-up-btn flex--item s-btn s-btn__unset c-pointer" data-controller="s-tooltip" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" data-selected-classes="fc-theme-primary" data-unselected-classes="" title="This answer is useful">
             <svg aria-hidden="true" class="svg-icon iconArrowUpLg" height="36" viewbox="0 0 36 36" width="36">
              <path d="M2 25h32L18 9 2 25Z">
              </path>
             </svg>
            </button>
            <div class="js-vote-count flex--item d-flex fd-column ai-center fc-black-500 fs-title" data-value="462" itemprop="upvoteCount">
             462
            </div>
            <button aria-label="Down vote" aria-pressed="false" class="js-vote-down-btn flex--item s-btn s-btn__unset c-pointer" data-controller="s-tooltip" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" data-selected-classes="fc-theme-primary" data-unselected-classes="" title="This answer is not useful">
             <svg aria-hidden="true" class="svg-icon iconArrowDownLg" height="36" viewbox="0 0 36 36" width="36">
              <path d="M2 11h32L18 27 2 11Z">
              </path>
             </svg>
            </button>
            <div aria-label="Accepted" class="js-accepted-answer-indicator flex--item fc-green-500 py6 mtn8 d-none" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" role="note" tabindex="0" title="Loading when this answer was accepted…">
             <div class="ta-center">
              <svg aria-hidden="true" class="svg-icon iconCheckmarkLg" height="36" viewbox="0 0 36 36" width="36">
               <path d="m6 14 8 8L30 6v8L14 30l-8-8v-8Z">
               </path>
              </svg>
             </div>
            </div>
            <a aria-label="Timeline" class="js-post-issue flex--item s-btn s-btn__unset c-pointer py6 mx-auto" data-controller="s-tooltip" data-ks-title="timeline" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" data-shortcut="T" href="/posts/38829074/timeline" title="Show activity on this post.">
             <svg aria-hidden="true" class="mln2 mr0 svg-icon iconHistory" height="18" viewbox="0 0 19 18" width="19">
              <path d="M3 9a8 8 0 1 1 3.73 6.77L8.2 14.3A6 6 0 1 0 5 9l3.01-.01-4 4-4-4h3L3 9Zm7-4h1.01L11 9.36l3.22 2.1-.6.93L10 10V5Z">
              </path>
             </svg>
            </a>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="answercell post-layout--right">
           <div class="s-prose js-post-body" itemprop="text">
            <p>
             How about a one-liner in JS
             <strong>
              ES10 / ES2019
             </strong>
             ?
            </p>
            <p>
             Making use of
             <a href="https://developer.mozilla.org/en/docs/Web/JavaScript/Reference/Global_Objects/Object/entries" rel="noreferrer">
              <code>
               Object.entries()
              </code>
             </a>
             and
             <a href="https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/JavaScript/Reference/Global_Objects/Object/fromEntries" rel="noreferrer">
              <code>
               Object.fromEntries()
              </code>
             </a>
             :
            </p>
            <pre class="lang-js prettyprint-override"><code>let newObj = Object.fromEntries(Object.entries(obj).map(([k, v]) =&gt; [k, v * v]));
</code></pre>
            <p>
             The same thing written as a function:
            </p>
            <pre class="lang-js prettyprint-override"><code>function objMap(obj, func) {
  return Object.fromEntries(Object.entries(obj).map(([k, v]) =&gt; [k, func(v)]));
}

// To square each value you can call it like this:
let mappedObj = objMap(obj, (x) =&gt; x * x);
</code></pre>
            <p>
             This function uses
             <em>
              recursion
             </em>
             to square nested objects as well:
            </p>
            <pre class="lang-js prettyprint-override"><code>function objMap(obj, func) {
  return Object.fromEntries(
    Object.entries(obj).map(([k, v]) =&gt; 
      [k, v === Object(v) ? objMap(v, func) : func(v)]
    )
  );
}

// To square each value you can call it like this:
let mappedObj = objMap(obj, (x) =&gt; x * x);
</code></pre>
            <p>
             With
             <strong>
              ES7 / ES2016
             </strong>
             you cant' use
             <code>
              Objects.fromEntries
             </code>
             , but you can achieve the same using
             <a href="https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/JavaScript/Reference/Global_Objects/Object/assign" rel="noreferrer">
              <code>
               Object.assign
              </code>
             </a>
             in combination with
             <a href="https://developer.mozilla.org/en/docs/Web/JavaScript/Reference/Operators/Spread_operator" rel="noreferrer">
              spread operators
             </a>
             and
             <a href="http://es6-features.org/#ComputedPropertyNames" rel="noreferrer">
              computed key names
             </a>
             syntax:
            </p>
            <pre class="lang-js prettyprint-override"><code>let newObj = Object.assign({}, ...Object.entries(obj).map(([k, v]) =&gt; ({[k]: v * v})));
</code></pre>
            <p>
             <strong>
              ES6 / ES2015
             </strong>
             Doesn't allow
             <code>
              Object.entries
             </code>
             , but you could use
             <a href="https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/JavaScript/Reference/Global_Objects/Object/keys" rel="noreferrer">
              <code>
               Object.keys
              </code>
             </a>
             instead:
            </p>
            <pre class="lang-js prettyprint-override"><code>let newObj = Object.assign({}, ...Object.keys(obj).map(k =&gt; ({[k]: obj[k] * obj[k]})));
</code></pre>
            <p>
             ES6 also introduced
             <a href="https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/JavaScript/Reference/Statements/for...of" rel="noreferrer">
              <code>
               for...of
              </code>
             </a>
             loops, which allow a more
             <em>
              imperative
             </em>
             style:
            </p>
            <pre class="lang-js prettyprint-override"><code>let newObj = {}

for (let [k, v] of Object.entries(obj)) {
  newObj[k] = v * v;
}
</code></pre>
            <hr/>
            <br/>
            <h3>
             array.reduce()
            </h3>
            <p>
             Instead of
             <code>
              Object.fromEntries
             </code>
             and
             <code>
              Object.assign
             </code>
             you can also use
             <a href="https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/JavaScript/Reference/Global_Objects/Array/reduce" rel="noreferrer">
              reduce
             </a>
             for this:
            </p>
            <pre class="lang-js prettyprint-override"><code>let newObj = Object.entries(obj).reduce((p, [k, v]) =&gt; ({ ...p, [k]: v * v }), {});
</code></pre>
            <hr/>
            <br/>
            <h3>
             Inherited properties and the prototype chain:
            </h3>
            <p>
             In some rare situation you may need to map a
             <em>
              class-like
             </em>
             object which holds properties of an inherited object on its
             <a href="https://developer.mozilla.org/en/docs/Web/JavaScript/Inheritance_and_the_prototype_chain" rel="noreferrer">
              prototype-chain
             </a>
             . In such cases
             <code>
              Object.keys()
             </code>
             and
             <code>
              Object.entries()
             </code>
             won't work, because these functions do not include the prototype chain.
            </p>
            <p>
             If you need to map
             <em>
              inherited
             </em>
             properties, you can use
             <code>
              for (key in myObj) {...}
             </code>
             .
            </p>
            <p>
             Here is an example of such situation:
            </p>
            <pre class="lang-js prettyprint-override"><code>const obj1 = { 'a': 1, 'b': 2, 'c': 3}
const obj2 = Object.create(obj1);  // One of multiple ways to inherit an object in JS.

// Here you see how the properties of obj1 sit on the 'prototype' of obj2
console.log(obj2)  // Prints: obj2.__proto__ = { 'a': 1, 'b': 2, 'c': 3}

console.log(Object.keys(obj2));  // Prints: an empty Array.
console.log(Object.entries(obj2));  // Prints: an empty Array.

for (let key in obj2) {
  console.log(key);              // Prints: 'a', 'b', 'c'
}
</code></pre>
            <p>
             However, please do me a favor and avoid
             <em>
              inheritance
             </em>
             . :-)
            </p>
           </div>

             <li class="comment js-comment" data-comment-id="100486239" data-comment-owner-id="688448" data-comment-score="1" id="comment-100486239">
              <div class="js-comment-actions comment-actions">
               <div class="comment-score js-comment-edit-hide">
                <span class="cool" title="number of 'useful comment' votes received">
                 1

               </div>

              <div class="comment-text js-comment-text-and-form">
               <div class="comment-body js-comment-edit-hide">
                <span class="comment-copy">
                 The solution
                 <code>
                  Object.assign(...Object.entries(obj).map(([k, v]) =&gt; ({[k]: v * v})))
                 </code>
                 does not work if
                 <code>
                  obj
                 </code>
                 is an empty object.  Change to:
                 <code>
                  Object.assign({}, ...Object.entries(obj).map(([k, v]) =&gt; ({[k]: v * v})))
                 </code>
                 .
                </span>
                <div class="d-inline-flex ai-center">
                 –
                 <a class="comment-user" href="/users/688448/blackcatweb" title="931 reputation">
                  blackcatweb
                 </a>

          <div class="votecell post-layout--left">
           <div class="js-voting-container d-flex jc-center fd-column ai-stretch gs4 fc-black-200" data-post-id="20663757">

          <div class="answercell post-layout--right">
           <div class="s-prose js-post-body" itemprop="text">
            <p>
             No native methods, but
             <a href="http://lodash.com/docs#mapValues" rel="noreferrer">
              lodash#mapValues
             </a>
             will do the job brilliantly
            </p>
            <pre><code>_.mapValues({ 'a': 1, 'b': 2, 'c': 3} , function(num) { return num * 3; });
// → { 'a': 3, 'b': 6, 'c': 9 }
</code></pre>
           </div>

               <div class="comment-body js-comment-edit-hide">
                <span class="comment-copy">
                 There is no need to add an extra HTTP call and an extra library just for one function. In any case, this answer is now outdated and you can simply call
                 <code>
                  Object.entries({a: 1, b: 2, c: 3})
                 </code>
                 to get an array.
                </span>
                <div class="d-inline-flex ai-center">

Also there’s no implied HTTP call in using Lodash, a popular library essentially built for this type of thing, although there’s quite a few things that ES6 has precluded the necessity of using utility function libraries to some degree lately.

             <li class="comment js-comment" data-comment-id="86105674" data-comment-owner-id="102960" data-comment-score="4" id="comment-86105674">
              <div class="js-comment-actions comment-actions">
               <div class="comment-score js-comment-edit-hide">
                <span class="cool" title="number of 'useful comment' votes received">
                 4
                </span>
               </div>
              </div>
              <div class="comment-text js-comment-text-and-form">
               <div class="comment-body js-comment-edit-hide">
                <span class="comment-copy">
                 extra HTTP call to pull Lodash, I guess. If this is your only use case, indeed it's an overkill. Nonetheless, it makes sense to have this answer around for Lodash is such a widespread library.
                </span>

               <div class="comment-body js-comment-edit-hide">
                <span class="comment-copy">
                 <code>
                  _.mapValues()
                 </code>
                 does also provide the key as the 2nd argument. Also
                 <code>
                  _.map()
                 </code>
                 would not work here as it only returns arrays, not objects:
                 <code>
                  _.map({ 'a': 1, 'b': 2, 'c': 3}, n =&gt; n * 3) // [3, 6, 9]
                 </code>
                </span>

         <div class="post-layout">
          <div class="votecell post-layout--left">
           <div class="js-voting-container d-flex jc-center fd-column ai-stretch gs4 fc-black-200" data-post-id="14810714">
            <button aria-label="Up vote" aria-pressed="false" class="js-vote-up-btn flex--item s-btn s-btn__unset c-pointer" data-controller="s-tooltip" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" data-selected-classes="fc-theme-primary" data-unselected-classes="" title="This answer is useful">
             <svg aria-hidden="true" class="svg-icon iconArrowUpLg" height="36" viewbox="0 0 36 36" width="36">
              <path d="M2 25h32L18 9 2 25Z">
              </path>
             </svg>
            </button>
            <div class="js-vote-count flex--item d-flex fd-column ai-center fc-black-500 fs-title" data-value="60" itemprop="upvoteCount">
             60
            </div>
            <button aria-label="Down vote" aria-pressed="false" class="js-vote-down-btn flex--item s-btn s-btn__unset c-pointer" data-controller="s-tooltip" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" data-selected-classes="fc-theme-primary" data-unselected-classes="" title="This answer is not useful">
             <svg aria-hidden="true" class="svg-icon iconArrowDownLg" height="36" viewbox="0 0 36 36" width="36">
              <path d="M2 11h32L18 27 2 11Z">
              </path>
             </svg>
            </button>
            <div aria-label="Accepted" class="js-accepted-answer-indicator flex--item fc-green-500 py6 mtn8 d-none" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" role="note" tabindex="0" title="Loading when this answer was accepted…">
             <div class="ta-center">
              <svg aria-hidden="true" class="svg-icon iconCheckmarkLg" height="36" viewbox="0 0 36 36" width="36">
               <path d="m6 14 8 8L30 6v8L14 30l-8-8v-8Z">
               </path>
              </svg>
             </div>
            </div>
            <a aria-label="Timeline" class="js-post-issue flex--item s-btn s-btn__unset c-pointer py6 mx-auto" data-controller="s-tooltip" data-ks-title="timeline" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" data-shortcut="T" href="/posts/14810714/timeline" title="Show activity on this post.">
             <svg aria-hidden="true" class="mln2 mr0 svg-icon iconHistory" height="18" viewbox="0 0 19 18" width="19">
              <path d="M3 9a8 8 0 1 1 3.73 6.77L8.2 14.3A6 6 0 1 0 5 9l3.01-.01-4 4-4-4h3L3 9Zm7-4h1.01L11 9.36l3.22 2.1-.6.93L10 10V5Z">
              </path>
             </svg>
            </a>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="answercell post-layout--right">
           <div class="s-prose js-post-body" itemprop="text">
            <p>
             It's pretty easy to write one:
            </p>
            <pre><code>Object.map = function(o, f, ctx) {
    ctx = ctx || this;
    var result = {};
    Object.keys(o).forEach(function(k) {
        result[k] = f.call(ctx, o[k], k, o); 
    });
    return result;
}
</code></pre>
            <p>
             with example code:
            </p>
            <pre><code>&gt; o = { a: 1, b: 2, c: 3 };
&gt; r = Object.map(o, function(v, k, o) {
     return v * v;
  });
&gt; r
{ a : 1, b: 4, c: 9 }
</code></pre>
            <p>
             NB: this version also allows you to (optionally) set the
             <code>
              this
             </code>
             context for the callback, just like the
             <code>
              Array
             </code>
             method.
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              EDIT
             </strong>
             - changed to remove use of
             <code>
              Object.prototype
             </code>
             , to ensure that it doesn't clash with any existing property named
             <code>
              map
             </code>
             on the object.
            </p>
           </div>

                 <code>
                  Object
                 </code>
                 that I think if ES ever did acquire this method it would be
                 <code>
                  Object.map
                 </code>
                 rather than
                 <code>
                  Object.prototype.map
                 </code>
                 (and this is also consistent with the other "static" methods on
                 <code>
                  Object
                 </code>
                 )

        <div class="answer js-answer" data-answerid="14810745" data-highest-scored="0" data-position-on-page="5" data-question-has-accepted-highest-score="1" data-score="26" id="answer-14810745" itemprop="suggestedAnswer" itemscope="" itemtype="https://schema.org/Answer">
         <div class="post-layout">
          <div class="votecell post-layout--left">
           <div class="js-voting-container d-flex jc-center fd-column ai-stretch gs4 fc-black-200" data-post-id="14810745">
            <button aria-label="Up vote" aria-pressed="false" class="js-vote-up-btn flex--item s-btn s-btn__unset c-pointer" data-controller="s-tooltip" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" data-selected-classes="fc-theme-primary" data-unselected-classes="" title="This answer is useful">

             </svg>

            </div>

             </svg>
            </button>
            <div aria-label="Accepted" class="js-accepted-answer-indicator flex--item fc-green-500 py6 mtn8 d-none" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" role="note" tabindex="0" title="Loading when this answer was accepted…">
             <div class="ta-center">
              <svg aria-hidden="true" class="svg-icon iconCheckmarkLg" height="36" viewbox="0 0 36 36" width="36">
               <path d="m6 14 8 8L30 6v8L14 30l-8-8v-8Z">
               </path>
              </svg>
             </div>
            </div>
            <a aria-label="Timeline" class="js-post-issue flex--item s-btn s-btn__unset c-pointer py6 mx-auto" data-controller="s-tooltip" data-ks-title="timeline" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" data-shortcut="T" href="/posts/14810745/timeline" title="Show activity on this post.">
             <svg aria-hidden="true" class="mln2 mr0 svg-icon iconHistory" height="18" viewbox="0 0 19 18" width="19">
              <path d="M3 9a8 8 0 1 1 3.73 6.77L8.2 14.3A6 6 0 1 0 5 9l3.01-.01-4 4-4-4h3L3 9Zm7-4h1.01L11 9.36l3.22 2.1-.6.93L10 10V5Z">
              </path>
             </svg>
            </a>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="answercell post-layout--right">
           <div class="s-prose js-post-body" itemprop="text">
            <p>
             You could use
             <a href="https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/JavaScript/Reference/Global_Objects/Object/keys">
              <code>
               Object.keys
              </code>
             </a>
             and then
             <code>
              forEach
             </code>
             over the returned array of keys:
            </p>
            <pre><code>var myObject = { 'a': 1, 'b': 2, 'c': 3 },
    newObject = {};
Object.keys(myObject).forEach(function (key) {
    var value = myObject[key];
    newObject[key] = value * value;
});
</code></pre>
            <p>
             Or in a more modular fashion:
            </p>
            <pre><code>function map(obj, callback) {
    var result = {};
    Object.keys(obj).forEach(function (key) {
        result[key] = callback.call(obj, obj[key], key, obj);
    });
    return result;
}

newObject = map(myObject, function(x) { return x * x; });
</code></pre>
            <p>
             Note that
             <code>
              Object.keys
             </code>
             returns an array containing only the object's own enumerable properties, thus it behaves like a
             <code>
              for..in
             </code>
             loop with a
             <code>
              hasOwnProperty
             </code>
             check.
            </p>
           </div>
           <div class="mt24">
            <div class="d-flex fw-wrap ai-start jc-end gs8 gsy">

        <a name="40008272">
        </a>
        <div class="answer js-answer" data-answerid="40008272" data-highest-scored="0" data-position-on-page="6" data-question-has-accepted-highest-score="1" data-score="25" id="answer-40008272" itemprop="suggestedAnswer" itemscope="" itemtype="https://schema.org/Answer">
         <div class="post-layout">
          <div class="votecell post-layout--left">
           <div class="js-voting-container d-flex jc-center fd-column ai-stretch gs4 fc-black-200" data-post-id="40008272">
            <button aria-label="Up vote" aria-pressed="false" class="js-vote-up-btn flex--item s-btn s-btn__unset c-pointer" data-controller="s-tooltip" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" data-selected-classes="fc-theme-primary" data-unselected-classes="" title="This answer is useful">
             <svg aria-hidden="true" class="svg-icon iconArrowUpLg" height="36" viewbox="0 0 36 36" width="36">
              <path d="M2 25h32L18 9 2 25Z">
              </path>
             </svg>
            </button>
            <div class="js-vote-count flex--item d-flex fd-column ai-center fc-black-500 fs-title" data-value="25" itemprop="upvoteCount">
             25
            </div>
            <button aria-label="Down vote" aria-pressed="false" class="js-vote-down-btn flex--item s-btn s-btn__unset c-pointer" data-controller="s-tooltip" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" data-selected-classes="fc-theme-primary" data-unselected-classes="" title="This answer is not useful">
             <svg aria-hidden="true" class="svg-icon iconArrowDownLg" height="36" viewbox="0 0 36 36" width="36">
              <path d="M2 11h32L18 27 2 11Z">
              </path>
             </svg>
            </button>
            <div aria-label="Accepted" class="js-accepted-answer-indicator flex--item fc-green-500 py6 mtn8 d-none" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" role="note" tabindex="0" title="Loading when this answer was accepted…">
             <div class="ta-center">
              <svg aria-hidden="true" class="svg-icon iconCheckmarkLg" height="36" viewbox="0 0 36 36" width="36">
               <path d="m6 14 8 8L30 6v8L14 30l-8-8v-8Z">
               </path>
              </svg>
             </div>
            </div>
            <a aria-label="Timeline" class="js-post-issue flex--item s-btn s-btn__unset c-pointer py6 mx-auto" data-controller="s-tooltip" data-ks-title="timeline" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" data-shortcut="T" href="/posts/40008272/timeline" title="Show activity on this post.">
             <svg aria-hidden="true" class="mln2 mr0 svg-icon iconHistory" height="18" viewbox="0 0 19 18" width="19">
              <path d="M3 9a8 8 0 1 1 3.73 6.77L8.2 14.3A6 6 0 1 0 5 9l3.01-.01-4 4-4-4h3L3 9Zm7-4h1.01L11 9.36l3.22 2.1-.6.93L10 10V5Z">
              </path>
             </svg>
            </a>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="answercell post-layout--right">
           <div class="s-prose js-post-body" itemprop="text">
            <p>
             This is really annoying, and everyone in the JS community knows it. There
             <em>
              should
             </em>
             be this functionality:
            </p>
            <pre><code>const obj1 = {a:4, b:7};
const obj2 = Object.map(obj1, (k,v) =&gt; v + 5);

console.log(obj1); // {a:4, b:7}
console.log(obj2); // {a:9, b:12}
</code></pre>
            <p>
             here is the naïve implementation:
            </p>
            <pre><code>Object.map = function(obj, fn, ctx){

    const ret = {};

    for(let k of Object.keys(obj)){
        ret[k] = fn.call(ctx || null, k, obj[k]);
    });

    return ret;
};
</code></pre>
            <p>
             it is super annoying to have to implement this yourself all the time ;)
            </p>
            <p>
             If you want something a little more sophisticated, that doesn't interfere with the Object class, try this:
            </p>
            <pre><code>let map = function (obj, fn, ctx) {
  return Object.keys(obj).reduce((a, b) =&gt; {
    a[b] = fn.call(ctx || null, b, obj[b]);
    return a;
  }, {});
};


const x = map({a: 2, b: 4}, (k,v) =&gt; {
    return v*2;
});
</code></pre>
            <p>
             but it is safe to add this map function to Object, just don't add to Object.prototype.
            </p>
            <pre><code>Object.map = ... // fairly safe
Object.prototype.map ... // not ok
</code></pre>
           </div>
           <div class="mt24">

               <div class="comment-body js-comment-edit-hide">
                <span class="comment-copy">
                 If map were just a random vague thing, sure.  But
                 <code>
                  .map
                 </code>
                 is generally understood as a Functor interface, and there's no single definition of Functor for "Object" because virtually anything in javascript can be an Object, including things with their own very distinct and defined .map interfaces/logic.
                </span>
                <div class="d-inline-flex ai-center">
                 –
                 <a class="comment-user" href="/users/1971194/dtipson" title="1,395 reputation">

                <span class="cool" title="number of 'useful comment' votes received">

                </span>

          <div class="answercell post-layout--right">
           <div class="s-prose js-post-body" itemprop="text">
            <p>
             I came here looking to find and answer for mapping an object to an array and got this page as a result. In case you came here looking for the same answer I was, here is how you can map and object to an array.
            </p>
            <p>
             You can use map to return a new array from the object like so:
            </p>
            <pre><code>var newObject = Object.keys(myObject).map(function(key) {
   return myObject[key];
});
</code></pre>
           </div>

        <a name="56110762">
        </a>
        <div class="answer js-answer" data-answerid="56110762" data-highest-scored="0" data-position-on-page="8" data-question-has-accepted-highest-score="1" data-score="17" id="answer-56110762" itemprop="suggestedAnswer" itemscope="" itemtype="https://schema.org/Answer">
         <div class="post-layout">
          <div class="votecell post-layout--left">
           <div class="js-voting-container d-flex jc-center fd-column ai-stretch gs4 fc-black-200" data-post-id="56110762">
            <button aria-label="Up vote" aria-pressed="false" class="js-vote-up-btn flex--item s-btn s-btn__unset c-pointer" data-controller="s-tooltip" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" data-selected-classes="fc-theme-primary" data-unselected-classes="" title="This answer is useful">
             <svg aria-hidden="true" class="svg-icon iconArrowUpLg" height="36" viewbox="0 0 36 36" width="36">
              <path d="M2 25h32L18 9 2 25Z">
              </path>
             </svg>
            </button>
            <div class="js-vote-count flex--item d-flex fd-column ai-center fc-black-500 fs-title" data-value="17" itemprop="upvoteCount">
             17
            </div>
            <button aria-label="Down vote" aria-pressed="false" class="js-vote-down-btn flex--item s-btn s-btn__unset c-pointer" data-controller="s-tooltip" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" data-selected-classes="fc-theme-primary" data-unselected-classes="" title="This answer is not useful">
             <svg aria-hidden="true" class="svg-icon iconArrowDownLg" height="36" viewbox="0 0 36 36" width="36">
              <path d="M2 11h32L18 27 2 11Z">
              </path>
             </svg>
            </button>
            <div aria-label="Accepted" class="js-accepted-answer-indicator flex--item fc-green-500 py6 mtn8 d-none" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" role="note" tabindex="0" title="Loading when this answer was accepted…">
             <div class="ta-center">
              <svg aria-hidden="true" class="svg-icon iconCheckmarkLg" height="36" viewbox="0 0 36 36" width="36">
               <path d="m6 14 8 8L30 6v8L14 30l-8-8v-8Z">
               </path>
              </svg>
             </div>
            </div>
            <a aria-label="Timeline" class="js-post-issue flex--item s-btn s-btn__unset c-pointer py6 mx-auto" data-controller="s-tooltip" data-ks-title="timeline" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" data-shortcut="T" href="/posts/56110762/timeline" title="Show activity on this post.">
             <svg aria-hidden="true" class="mln2 mr0 svg-icon iconHistory" height="18" viewbox="0 0 19 18" width="19">
              <path d="M3 9a8 8 0 1 1 3.73 6.77L8.2 14.3A6 6 0 1 0 5 9l3.01-.01-4 4-4-4h3L3 9Zm7-4h1.01L11 9.36l3.22 2.1-.6.93L10 10V5Z">
              </path>
             </svg>
            </a>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="answercell post-layout--right">
           <div class="s-prose js-post-body" itemprop="text">
            <p>
             JavaScript just got the new
             <code>
              Object.fromEntries
             </code>
             method.
            </p>
            <h2>
             Example
            </h2>
            <p>
             <div class="snippet" data-babel="false" data-console="true" data-hide="false" data-lang="js">
              <div class="snippet-code">
               <pre class="snippet-code-js lang-js prettyprint-override"><code>function mapObject (obj, fn) {
  return Object.fromEntries(
    Object
      .entries(obj)
      .map(fn)
  )
}

const myObject = { a: 1, b: 2, c: 3 }
const myNewObject = mapObject(myObject, ([key, value]) =&gt; ([key, value * value]))
console.log(myNewObject)</code></pre>
              </div>
             </div>
            </p>
            <h2>
             Explanation
            </h2>
            <p>
             The code above converts the Object into an nested Array (
             <code>
              [[&lt;key&gt;,&lt;value&gt;], ...]
             </code>
             ) wich you can map over.
             <code>
              Object.fromEntries
             </code>
             converts the Array back to an Object.
            </p>
            <p>
             The cool thing about this pattern, is that you can now easily take object keys into account while mapping.
            </p>
            <h2>
             Documentation
            </h2>
            <ul>
             <li>
              <a href="https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/JavaScript/Reference/Global_Objects/Object/fromEntries" rel="noreferrer">
               <code>
                Object.fromEntries()
               </code>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/JavaScript/Reference/Global_Objects/Object/entries" rel="noreferrer">
               <code>
                Object.entries()
               </code>
              </a>
             </li>
            </ul>
            <h2>
             Browser Support
            </h2>
            <p>
             <code>
              Object.fromEntries
             </code>
             is currently only supported by
             <a href="https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/JavaScript/Reference/Global_Objects/Object/fromEntries#Browser_compatibility" rel="noreferrer">
              these browsers/engines
             </a>
             , nevertheless there are polyfills available (e.g
             <a href="https://babeljs.io/docs/en/babel-polyfill" rel="noreferrer">
              @babel/polyfill
             </a>
             ).
            </p>
           </div>
           <div class="mt24">
            <div class="d-flex fw-wrap ai-start jc-end gs8 gsy">

              <div class="comment-text js-comment-text-and-form">
               <div class="comment-body js-comment-edit-hide">
                <span class="comment-copy">
                 Basically,
                 <code>
                  Object.fromEntries
                 </code>
                 is the opposite of
                 <code>
                  Object.entries
                 </code>
                 .
                 <code>
                  Object.entries
                 </code>
                 converts an object to a list of key-value pairs.
                 <code>
                  Object.fromEntries
                 </code>
                 converts a list of key-value pairs to an object.
                </span>
                <div class="d-inline-flex ai-center">
                 –
                 <a class="comment-user" href="/users/450913/orad" title="13,803 reputation">

              <div class="comment-text js-comment-text-and-form">
               <div class="comment-body js-comment-edit-hide">
                <span class="comment-copy">
                 Not a bad solution. Clean and simple. Except function params are different to
                 <code>
                  Array.map()
                 </code>
                 . My preference would be for the map function params to be
                 <code>
                  (value, key)
                 </code>
                 . I know this seems somewhat backwards, however that's the order used for
                 <code>
                  Array.map()
                 </code>
                 and
                 <code>
                  Array.forEach()
                 </code>
                 so it's more consistent.
                </span>
                <div class="d-inline-flex ai-center">
                 –

        <div class="answer js-answer" data-answerid="38753295" data-highest-scored="0" data-position-on-page="9" data-question-has-accepted-highest-score="1" data-score="14" id="answer-38753295" itemprop="suggestedAnswer" itemscope="" itemtype="https://schema.org/Answer">
         <div class="post-layout">
          <div class="votecell post-layout--left">
           <div class="js-voting-container d-flex jc-center fd-column ai-stretch gs4 fc-black-200" data-post-id="38753295">
            <button aria-label="Up vote" aria-pressed="false" class="js-vote-up-btn flex--item s-btn s-btn__unset c-pointer" data-controller="s-tooltip" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" data-selected-classes="fc-theme-primary" data-unselected-classes="" title="This answer is useful">

            </div>

             <svg aria-hidden="true" class="svg-icon iconArrowDownLg" height="36" viewbox="0 0 36 36" width="36">

             </svg>

          <div class="answercell post-layout--right">
           <div class="s-prose js-post-body" itemprop="text">
            <p>
             The accepted answer has two drawbacks:
            </p>
            <ul>
             <li>
              It misuses
              <code>
               Array.prototype.reduce
              </code>
              , because reducing means to change the structure of a composite type, which doesn't happen in this case.
             </li>
             <li>
              It is not particularly reusable
             </li>
            </ul>
            <hr/>
            <h3>
             An ES6/ES2015 functional approach
            </h3>
            <p>
             Please note that all functions are defined in curried form.
            </p>
            <p>
             <div class="snippet" data-babel="false" data-console="true" data-hide="false" data-lang="js">
              <div class="snippet-code">
               <pre class="snippet-code-js lang-js prettyprint-override"><code>// small, reusable auxiliary functions

const keys = o =&gt; Object.keys(o);

const assign = (...o) =&gt; Object.assign({}, ...o);

const map = f =&gt; xs =&gt; xs.map(x =&gt; f(x));

const mul = y =&gt; x =&gt; x * y;

const sqr = x =&gt; mul(x) (x);


// the actual map function

const omap = f =&gt; o =&gt; {
  o = assign(o); // A
  map(x =&gt; o[x] = f(o[x])) (keys(o)); // B
  return o;
};


// mock data

const o = {"a":1, "b":2, "c":3};


// and run

console.log(omap(sqr) (o));
console.log(omap(mul(10)) (o));</code></pre>
              </div>
             </div>
            </p>
            <ul>
             <li>
              In line A
              <code>
               o
              </code>
              is reassigned. Since Javascript passes reference values
              <a href="https://stackoverflow.com/a/38533677/6445533">
               by sharing
              </a>
              , a shallow copy of
              <code>
               o
              </code>
              is generated. We are now able to mutate
              <code>
               o
              </code>
              within
              <code>
               omap
              </code>
              without mutating
              <code>
               o
              </code>
              in the parent scope.
             </li>
             <li>
              In line B
              <code>
               map
              </code>
              's return value is ignored, because
              <code>
               map
              </code>
              performs a mutation of
              <code>
               o
              </code>
              . Since this side effect remains within
              <code>
               omap
              </code>
              and isn't visible in the parent scope, it is totally acceptable.
             </li>
            </ul>
            <p>
             This is not the fastest solution, but a declarative and reusable one. Here is the same implementation as a one-line, succinct but less readable:
            </p>
            <pre><code>const omap = f =&gt; o =&gt; (o = assign(o), map(x =&gt; o[x] = f(o[x])) (keys(o)), o);
</code></pre>
            <hr/>
            <h3>
             Addendum - why are objects not iterable by default?
            </h3>
            <p>
             ES2015 specified the iterator and iterable protocols. But objects are still not iterable and thus not mappable.
             <a href="https://stackoverflow.com/a/38777177/6445533">
              The reason is the mixing of data and program level
             </a>
             .
            </p>
           </div>

             <li class="comment js-comment" data-comment-id="77104112" data-comment-owner-id="1971194" data-comment-score="2" id="comment-77104112">
              <div class="js-comment-actions comment-actions">
               <div class="comment-score js-comment-edit-hide">
                <span class="cool" title="number of 'useful comment' votes received">

              <div class="comment-text js-comment-text-and-form">
               <div class="comment-body js-comment-edit-hide">
                <span class="comment-copy">
                 "reducing means to change the structure of a composite type" I don't think that's true. An Array.reduce that produces a new array of the exact same length or even the exact same values is perfectly legitimate.  Reduce can be use to re-create the functionality of map and/or filter (or both, as in a complex transducer, for which reduce is the basis). In FP, it's a type of fold, and a fold that ends up with the same type is still a fold.
                </span>
                <div class="d-inline-flex ai-center">
                 –
                 <a class="comment-user" href="/users/1971194/dtipson" title="1,395 reputation">
                  Dtipson
                 </a>

                </span>
               </div>
              </div>
             </li>
             <li class="comment js-comment" data-comment-id="77104495" data-comment-owner-id="-1" data-comment-score="2" id="comment-77104495">
              <div class="js-comment-actions comment-actions">
               <div class="comment-score js-comment-edit-hide">
                <span class="cool" title="number of 'useful comment' votes received">
                 2
                </span>
               </div>
              </div>
              <div class="comment-text js-comment-text-and-form">
               <div class="comment-body js-comment-edit-hide">
                <span class="comment-copy">
                 @Dtipson You're absolutely right. A
                 <code>
                  fold
                 </code>
                 is more generic than a
                 <code>
                  map
                 </code>
                 (functor). However, this was my knowledge from mid-2016. That's half an eternity :D
                </span>

          <div class="answercell post-layout--right">
           <div class="s-prose js-post-body" itemprop="text">
            <h1>
             Minimal version
            </h1>
            <h2>
             ES2017
            </h2>
            <pre class="lang-js prettyprint-override"><code>Object.entries(obj).reduce((a, [k, v]) =&gt; (a[k] = v * v, a), {})
                                                  ↑↑↑↑↑
</code></pre>
            <h2>
             ES2019
            </h2>
            <pre class="lang-js prettyprint-override"><code>Object.fromEntries(Object.entries(obj).map(([k, v]) =&gt; [k, v * v]))
                                                           ↑↑↑↑↑
</code></pre>
           </div>

        <a name="61040133">
        </a>
        <div class="answer js-answer" data-answerid="61040133" data-highest-scored="0" data-position-on-page="11" data-question-has-accepted-highest-score="1" data-score="10" id="answer-61040133" itemprop="suggestedAnswer" itemscope="" itemtype="https://schema.org/Answer">
         <div class="post-layout">
          <div class="votecell post-layout--left">
           <div class="js-voting-container d-flex jc-center fd-column ai-stretch gs4 fc-black-200" data-post-id="61040133">
            <button aria-label="Up vote" aria-pressed="false" class="js-vote-up-btn flex--item s-btn s-btn__unset c-pointer" data-controller="s-tooltip" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" data-selected-classes="fc-theme-primary" data-unselected-classes="" title="This answer is useful">
             <svg aria-hidden="true" class="svg-icon iconArrowUpLg" height="36" viewbox="0 0 36 36" width="36">
              <path d="M2 25h32L18 9 2 25Z">
              </path>
             </svg>
            </button>
            <div class="js-vote-count flex--item d-flex fd-column ai-center fc-black-500 fs-title" data-value="10" itemprop="upvoteCount">
             10
            </div>
            <button aria-label="Down vote" aria-pressed="false" class="js-vote-down-btn flex--item s-btn s-btn__unset c-pointer" data-controller="s-tooltip" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" data-selected-classes="fc-theme-primary" data-unselected-classes="" title="This answer is not useful">
             <svg aria-hidden="true" class="svg-icon iconArrowDownLg" height="36" viewbox="0 0 36 36" width="36">
              <path d="M2 11h32L18 27 2 11Z">
              </path>
             </svg>
            </button>
            <div aria-label="Accepted" class="js-accepted-answer-indicator flex--item fc-green-500 py6 mtn8 d-none" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" role="note" tabindex="0" title="Loading when this answer was accepted…">
             <div class="ta-center">
              <svg aria-hidden="true" class="svg-icon iconCheckmarkLg" height="36" viewbox="0 0 36 36" width="36">
               <path d="m6 14 8 8L30 6v8L14 30l-8-8v-8Z">
               </path>
              </svg>
             </div>
            </div>
            <a aria-label="Timeline" class="js-post-issue flex--item s-btn s-btn__unset c-pointer py6 mx-auto" data-controller="s-tooltip" data-ks-title="timeline" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" data-shortcut="T" href="/posts/61040133/timeline" title="Show activity on this post.">
             <svg aria-hidden="true" class="mln2 mr0 svg-icon iconHistory" height="18" viewbox="0 0 19 18" width="19">
              <path d="M3 9a8 8 0 1 1 3.73 6.77L8.2 14.3A6 6 0 1 0 5 9l3.01-.01-4 4-4-4h3L3 9Zm7-4h1.01L11 9.36l3.22 2.1-.6.93L10 10V5Z">
              </path>
             </svg>
            </a>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="answercell post-layout--right">
           <div class="s-prose js-post-body" itemprop="text">
            <p>
             You can convert an object to array simply by using the following:
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              You can convert the object values to an array:
             </strong>
            </p>
            <p>
             <div class="snippet" data-babel="false" data-console="true" data-hide="false" data-lang="js">
              <div class="snippet-code">
               <pre class="snippet-code-js lang-js prettyprint-override"><code>myObject = { 'a': 1, 'b': 2, 'c': 3 };

let valuesArray = Object.values(myObject);

console.log(valuesArray);</code></pre>
              </div>
             </div>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              You can convert the object keys to an array:
             </strong>
            </p>
            <p>
             <div class="snippet" data-babel="false" data-console="true" data-hide="false" data-lang="js">
              <div class="snippet-code">
               <pre class="snippet-code-js lang-js prettyprint-override"><code>myObject = { 'a': 1, 'b': 2, 'c': 3 };

let keysArray = Object.keys(myObject);

console.log(keysArray);</code></pre>
              </div>
             </div>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Now you can perform normal array operations, including the 'map' function
             </strong>
            </p>
           </div>
           <div class="mt24">
            <div class="d-flex fw-wrap ai-start jc-end gs8 gsy">
             <time datetime="2020-04-05T08:53:12" itemprop="dateCreated">
             </time>
             <div class="flex--item mr16" style="flex: 1 1 100px;">
              <div class="js-post-menu pt2" data-post-id="61040133">

         <div class="post-layout">
          <div class="votecell post-layout--left">
           <div class="js-voting-container d-flex jc-center fd-column ai-stretch gs4 fc-black-200" data-post-id="39829388">
            <button aria-label="Up vote" aria-pressed="false" class="js-vote-up-btn flex--item s-btn s-btn__unset c-pointer" data-controller="s-tooltip" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" data-selected-classes="fc-theme-primary" data-unselected-classes="" title="This answer is useful">

              </path>

            <div class="js-vote-count flex--item d-flex fd-column ai-center fc-black-500 fs-title" data-value="8" itemprop="upvoteCount">
             8
            </div>
            <button aria-label="Down vote" aria-pressed="false" class="js-vote-down-btn flex--item s-btn s-btn__unset c-pointer" data-controller="s-tooltip" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" data-selected-classes="fc-theme-primary" data-unselected-classes="" title="This answer is not useful">
             <svg aria-hidden="true" class="svg-icon iconArrowDownLg" height="36" viewbox="0 0 36 36" width="36">
              <path d="M2 11h32L18 27 2 11Z">
              </path>
             </svg>
            </button>
            <div aria-label="Accepted" class="js-accepted-answer-indicator flex--item fc-green-500 py6 mtn8 d-none" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" role="note" tabindex="0" title="Loading when this answer was accepted…">
             <div class="ta-center">
              <svg aria-hidden="true" class="svg-icon iconCheckmarkLg" height="36" viewbox="0 0 36 36" width="36">
               <path d="m6 14 8 8L30 6v8L14 30l-8-8v-8Z">
               </path>
              </svg>
             </div>
            </div>
            <a aria-label="Timeline" class="js-post-issue flex--item s-btn s-btn__unset c-pointer py6 mx-auto" data-controller="s-tooltip" data-ks-title="timeline" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" data-shortcut="T" href="/posts/39829388/timeline" title="Show activity on this post.">
             <svg aria-hidden="true" class="mln2 mr0 svg-icon iconHistory" height="18" viewbox="0 0 19 18" width="19">
              <path d="M3 9a8 8 0 1 1 3.73 6.77L8.2 14.3A6 6 0 1 0 5 9l3.01-.01-4 4-4-4h3L3 9Zm7-4h1.01L11 9.36l3.22 2.1-.6.93L10 10V5Z">

             </svg>
            </a>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="answercell post-layout--right">
           <div class="s-prose js-post-body" itemprop="text">
            <p>
             For maximum performance.
            </p>
            <p>
             If your object doesn't change often but needs to be iterated on often I suggest using a native Map as a cache.
            </p>
            <p>
             <div class="snippet" data-babel="false" data-console="true" data-hide="false" data-lang="js">
              <div class="snippet-code">
               <pre class="snippet-code-js lang-js prettyprint-override"><code>// example object
var obj = {a: 1, b: 2, c: 'something'};

// caching map
var objMap = new Map(Object.entries(obj));

// fast iteration on Map object
objMap.forEach((item, key) =&gt; {
  // do something with an item
  console.log(key, item);
});</code></pre>
              </div>
             </div>
            </p>
            <p>
             Object.entries already works in Chrome, Edge, Firefox and beta Opera so it's a future-proof feature.
It's from ES7 so polyfill it
             <a href="https://github.com/es-shims/Object.entries" rel="noreferrer">
              https://github.com/es-shims/Object.entries
             </a>
             for IE where it doesn't work.
            </p>
           </div>

        <a name="52568181">
        </a>
        <div class="answer js-answer" data-answerid="52568181" data-highest-scored="0" data-position-on-page="13" data-question-has-accepted-highest-score="1" data-score="8" id="answer-52568181" itemprop="suggestedAnswer" itemscope="" itemtype="https://schema.org/Answer">
         <div class="post-layout">
          <div class="votecell post-layout--left">
           <div class="js-voting-container d-flex jc-center fd-column ai-stretch gs4 fc-black-200" data-post-id="52568181">
            <button aria-label="Up vote" aria-pressed="false" class="js-vote-up-btn flex--item s-btn s-btn__unset c-pointer" data-controller="s-tooltip" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" data-selected-classes="fc-theme-primary" data-unselected-classes="" title="This answer is useful">
             <svg aria-hidden="true" class="svg-icon iconArrowUpLg" height="36" viewbox="0 0 36 36" width="36">
              <path d="M2 25h32L18 9 2 25Z">
              </path>
             </svg>
            </button>
            <div class="js-vote-count flex--item d-flex fd-column ai-center fc-black-500 fs-title" data-value="8" itemprop="upvoteCount">
             8
            </div>
            <button aria-label="Down vote" aria-pressed="false" class="js-vote-down-btn flex--item s-btn s-btn__unset c-pointer" data-controller="s-tooltip" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" data-selected-classes="fc-theme-primary" data-unselected-classes="" title="This answer is not useful">
             <svg aria-hidden="true" class="svg-icon iconArrowDownLg" height="36" viewbox="0 0 36 36" width="36">
              <path d="M2 11h32L18 27 2 11Z">
              </path>
             </svg>
            </button>
            <div aria-label="Accepted" class="js-accepted-answer-indicator flex--item fc-green-500 py6 mtn8 d-none" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" role="note" tabindex="0" title="Loading when this answer was accepted…">
             <div class="ta-center">
              <svg aria-hidden="true" class="svg-icon iconCheckmarkLg" height="36" viewbox="0 0 36 36" width="36">
               <path d="m6 14 8 8L30 6v8L14 30l-8-8v-8Z">
               </path>
              </svg>
             </div>
            </div>
            <a aria-label="Timeline" class="js-post-issue flex--item s-btn s-btn__unset c-pointer py6 mx-auto" data-controller="s-tooltip" data-ks-title="timeline" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" data-shortcut="T" href="/posts/52568181/timeline" title="Show activity on this post.">
             <svg aria-hidden="true" class="mln2 mr0 svg-icon iconHistory" height="18" viewbox="0 0 19 18" width="19">
              <path d="M3 9a8 8 0 1 1 3.73 6.77L8.2 14.3A6 6 0 1 0 5 9l3.01-.01-4 4-4-4h3L3 9Zm7-4h1.01L11 9.36l3.22 2.1-.6.93L10 10V5Z">
              </path>
             </svg>
            </a>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="answercell post-layout--right">
           <div class="s-prose js-post-body" itemprop="text">
            <p>
             you can use
             <code>
              map
             </code>
             method and
             <code>
              forEach
             </code>
             on arrays but if you want to use it on
             <code>
              Object
             </code>
             then you can use it with twist like below:
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Using Javascript (ES6)
             </strong>
            </p>
            <pre><code>var obj = { 'a': 2, 'b': 4, 'c': 6 };   
Object.entries(obj).map( v =&gt; obj[v[0]] *= v[1] );
console.log(obj); //it will log as {a: 4, b: 16, c: 36}

var obj2 = { 'a': 4, 'b': 8, 'c': 10 };
Object.entries(obj2).forEach( v =&gt; obj2[v[0]] *= v[1] );
console.log(obj2); //it will log as {a: 16, b: 64, c: 100}
</code></pre>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Using jQuery
             </strong>
            </p>
            <pre><code>var ob = { 'a': 2, 'b': 4, 'c': 6 };
$.map(ob, function (val, key) {
   ob[key] *= val;
});
console.log(ob) //it will log as {a: 4, b: 16, c: 36}
</code></pre>
            <p>
             Or you can use other loops also like
             <code>
              $.each
             </code>
             method as below example:
            </p>
            <pre><code>$.each(ob,function (key, value) {
  ob[key] *= value;
});
console.log(ob) //it will also log as {a: 4, b: 16, c: 36}
</code></pre>
           </div>
           <div class="mt24">
            <div class="d-flex fw-wrap ai-start jc-end gs8 gsy">
             <time datetime="2018-09-29T12:03:26" itemprop="dateCreated">
             </time>
             <div class="flex--item mr16" style="flex: 1 1 100px;">
              <div class="js-post-menu pt2" data-post-id="52568181">
               <div class="d-flex gs8 s-anchors s-anchors__muted fw-wrap">
                <div class="flex--item">

         <div class="post-layout">
          <div class="votecell post-layout--left">
           <div class="js-voting-container d-flex jc-center fd-column ai-stretch gs4 fc-black-200" data-post-id="14810690">
            <button aria-label="Up vote" aria-pressed="false" class="js-vote-up-btn flex--item s-btn s-btn__unset c-pointer" data-controller="s-tooltip" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" data-selected-classes="fc-theme-primary" data-unselected-classes="" title="This answer is useful">
             <svg aria-hidden="true" class="svg-icon iconArrowUpLg" height="36" viewbox="0 0 36 36" width="36">
              <path d="M2 25h32L18 9 2 25Z">
              </path>
             </svg>
            </button>
            <div class="js-vote-count flex--item d-flex fd-column ai-center fc-black-500 fs-title" data-value="7" itemprop="upvoteCount">
             7
            </div>
            <button aria-label="Down vote" aria-pressed="false" class="js-vote-down-btn flex--item s-btn s-btn__unset c-pointer" data-controller="s-tooltip" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" data-selected-classes="fc-theme-primary" data-unselected-classes="" title="This answer is not useful">
             <svg aria-hidden="true" class="svg-icon iconArrowDownLg" height="36" viewbox="0 0 36 36" width="36">
              <path d="M2 11h32L18 27 2 11Z">
              </path>
             </svg>
            </button>
            <div aria-label="Accepted" class="js-accepted-answer-indicator flex--item fc-green-500 py6 mtn8 d-none" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" role="note" tabindex="0" title="Loading when this answer was accepted…">
             <div class="ta-center">
              <svg aria-hidden="true" class="svg-icon iconCheckmarkLg" height="36" viewbox="0 0 36 36" width="36">
               <path d="m6 14 8 8L30 6v8L14 30l-8-8v-8Z">
               </path>
              </svg>
             </div>
            </div>
            <a aria-label="Timeline" class="js-post-issue flex--item s-btn s-btn__unset c-pointer py6 mx-auto" data-controller="s-tooltip" data-ks-title="timeline" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" data-shortcut="T" href="/posts/14810690/timeline" title="Show activity on this post.">
             <svg aria-hidden="true" class="mln2 mr0 svg-icon iconHistory" height="18" viewbox="0 0 19 18" width="19">
              <path d="M3 9a8 8 0 1 1 3.73 6.77L8.2 14.3A6 6 0 1 0 5 9l3.01-.01-4 4-4-4h3L3 9Zm7-4h1.01L11 9.36l3.22 2.1-.6.93L10 10V5Z">

          <div class="answercell post-layout--right">
           <div class="s-prose js-post-body" itemprop="text">
            <p>
             The
             <code>
              map function
             </code>
             does not exist on the
             <code>
              Object.prototype
             </code>
             however you can emulate it like so
            </p>
            <pre><code>var myMap = function ( obj, callback ) {

    var result = {};

    for ( var key in obj ) {
        if ( Object.prototype.hasOwnProperty.call( obj, key ) ) {
            if ( typeof callback === 'function' ) {
                result[ key ] = callback.call( obj, obj[ key ], key, obj );
            }
        }
    }

    return result;

};

var myObject = { 'a': 1, 'b': 2, 'c': 3 };

var newObject = myMap( myObject, function ( value, key ) {
    return value * value;
});
</code></pre>
           </div>

           <div class="comments js-comments-container bt bc-black-075 mt12" data-min-length="15" data-post-id="14810690" id="comments-14810690">
            <ul class="comments-list js-comments-list" data-addlink-disabled="true" data-canpost="false" data-cansee="true" data-comments-unavailable="false" data-remaining-comments-count="0">
             <li class="comment js-comment" data-comment-id="58599022" data-comment-owner-id="2109067" data-comment-score="0" id="comment-58599022">
              <div class="js-comment-actions comment-actions">
               <div class="comment-score js-comment-edit-hide">
               </div>
              </div>
              <div class="comment-text js-comment-text-and-form">
               <div class="comment-body js-comment-edit-hide">
                <span class="comment-copy">
                 Perfomance issues:
                 <code>
                  typeof callback === 'function'
                 </code>
                 absolutely redundant. 1)
                 <code>
                  map
                 </code>
                 has no meaning without callback 2) if
                 <code>
                  callback
                 </code>
                 isn't function, yours
                 <code>
                  map
                 </code>
                 implementation just runs meaningless for-loop. Also,
                 <code>
                  Object.prototype.hasOwnProperty.call( obj, key )
                 </code>
                 is a bit overkill.
                </span>
                <div class="d-inline-flex ai-center">
                 –
                 <a class="comment-user" href="/users/2109067/ankhzet" title="2,406 reputation">
                  ankhzet
                 </a>
                </div>
