        <a name="38843306">
        </a>
        <div class="answer js-answer" data-answerid="38843306" data-highest-scored="0" data-position-on-page="15" data-question-has-accepted-highest-score="1" data-score="6" id="answer-38843306" itemprop="suggestedAnswer" itemscope="" itemtype="https://schema.org/Answer">
         <div class="post-layout">
          <div class="votecell post-layout--left">
           <div class="js-voting-container d-flex jc-center fd-column ai-stretch gs4 fc-black-200" data-post-id="38843306">
            <button aria-label="Up vote" aria-pressed="false" class="js-vote-up-btn flex--item s-btn s-btn__unset c-pointer" data-controller="s-tooltip" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" data-selected-classes="fc-theme-primary" data-unselected-classes="" title="This answer is useful">
             <svg aria-hidden="true" class="svg-icon iconArrowUpLg" height="36" viewbox="0 0 36 36" width="36">
              <path d="M2 25h32L18 9 2 25Z">
              </path>
             </svg>
            </button>
            <div class="js-vote-count flex--item d-flex fd-column ai-center fc-black-500 fs-title" data-value="6" itemprop="upvoteCount">
             6
            </div>
            <button aria-label="Down vote" aria-pressed="false" class="js-vote-down-btn flex--item s-btn s-btn__unset c-pointer" data-controller="s-tooltip" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" data-selected-classes="fc-theme-primary" data-unselected-classes="" title="This answer is not useful">
             <svg aria-hidden="true" class="svg-icon iconArrowDownLg" height="36" viewbox="0 0 36 36" width="36">
              <path d="M2 11h32L18 27 2 11Z">
              </path>
             </svg>
            </button>
            <div aria-label="Accepted" class="js-accepted-answer-indicator flex--item fc-green-500 py6 mtn8 d-none" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" role="note" tabindex="0" title="Loading when this answer was accepted…">
             <div class="ta-center">
              <svg aria-hidden="true" class="svg-icon iconCheckmarkLg" height="36" viewbox="0 0 36 36" width="36">
               <path d="m6 14 8 8L30 6v8L14 30l-8-8v-8Z">
               </path>
              </svg>
             </div>
            </div>
            <a aria-label="Timeline" class="js-post-issue flex--item s-btn s-btn__unset c-pointer py6 mx-auto" data-controller="s-tooltip" data-ks-title="timeline" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" data-shortcut="T" href="/posts/38843306/timeline" title="Show activity on this post.">
             <svg aria-hidden="true" class="mln2 mr0 svg-icon iconHistory" height="18" viewbox="0 0 19 18" width="19">
              <path d="M3 9a8 8 0 1 1 3.73 6.77L8.2 14.3A6 6 0 1 0 5 9l3.01-.01-4 4-4-4h3L3 9Zm7-4h1.01L11 9.36l3.22 2.1-.6.93L10 10V5Z">
              </path>
             </svg>
            </a>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="answercell post-layout--right">
           <div class="s-prose js-post-body" itemprop="text">
            <p>
             EDIT: The canonical way using newer JavaScript features is -
            </p>
            <pre><code>const identity = x =&gt;
  x

const omap = (f = identity, o = {}) =&gt;
  Object.fromEntries(
    Object.entries(o).map(([ k, v ]) =&gt;
      [ k, f(v) ]
    )
  )
</code></pre>
            <p>
             Where
             <code>
              o
             </code>
             is some object and
             <code>
              f
             </code>
             is your mapping function. Or we could say, given a function from
             <code>
              a -&gt; b
             </code>
             , and an object with values of type
             <code>
              a
             </code>
             , produce an object with values of type
             <code>
              b
             </code>
             . As a pseudo type signature -
            </p>
            <pre><code>// omap : (a -&gt; b, { a }) -&gt; { b }
</code></pre>
            <hr/>
            <p>
             The original answer was written to demonstrate a powerful combinator,
             <code>
              mapReduce
             </code>
             which allows us to think of our transformation in a different way
            </p>
            <ol>
             <li>
              <code>
               m
              </code>
              , the
              <em>
               mapping
              </em>
              function – gives you a chance to transform the incoming element before…
             </li>
             <li>
              <code>
               r
              </code>
              , the
              <em>
               reducing
              </em>
              function – this function combines the accumulator with the result of the mapped element
             </li>
            </ol>
            <p>
             Intuitively,
             <code>
              mapReduce
             </code>
             creates a new reducer we can plug directly into
             <code>
              Array.prototype.reduce
             </code>
             . But more importantly, we can implement our object functor implementation
             <code>
              omap
             </code>
             plainly by utilizing the object monoid,
             <code>
              Object.assign
             </code>
             and
             <code>
              {}
             </code>
             .
            </p>
            <p>
             <div class="snippet" data-babel="false" data-console="true" data-hide="false" data-lang="js">
              <div class="snippet-code">
               <pre class="snippet-code-js lang-js prettyprint-override"><code>const identity = x =&gt;
  x
  
const mapReduce = (m, r) =&gt;
  (a, x) =&gt; r (a, m (x))

const omap = (f = identity, o = {}) =&gt;
  Object
    .keys (o)
    .reduce
      ( mapReduce
          ( k =&gt; ({ [k]: f (o[k]) })
          , Object.assign
          )
      , {}
      )
          
const square = x =&gt;
  x * x
  
const data =
  { a : 1, b : 2, c : 3 }
  
console .log (omap (square, data))
// { a : 1, b : 4, c : 9 }</code></pre>
              </div>
             </div>
            </p>
            <p>
             Notice the only part of the program we actually had to write is the mapping implementation itself –
            </p>
            <pre><code>k =&gt; ({ [k]: f (o[k]) })
</code></pre>
            <p>
             Which says, given a known object
             <code>
              o
             </code>
             and some key
             <code>
              k
             </code>
             , construct an object and whose computed property
             <code>
              k
             </code>
             is the result of calling
             <code>
              f
             </code>
             on the key's value,
             <code>
              o[k]
             </code>
             .
            </p>
            <p>
             We get a glimpse of
             <code>
              mapReduce
             </code>
             's sequencing potential if we first abstract
             <code>
              oreduce
             </code>
            </p>
            <pre><code>// oreduce : (string * a -&gt; string * b, b, { a }) -&gt; { b }
const oreduce = (f = identity, r = null, o = {}) =&gt;
  Object
    .keys (o)
    .reduce
      ( mapReduce
          ( k =&gt; [ k, o[k] ]
          , f
          )
      , r
      )

// omap : (a -&gt; b, {a}) -&gt; {b}
const omap = (f = identity, o = {}) =&gt;
  oreduce
    ( mapReduce
        ( ([ k, v ]) =&gt;
            ({ [k]: f (v) })
        , Object.assign
        )
    , {}
    , o
    )
</code></pre>
            <p>
             Everything works the same, but
             <code>
              omap
             </code>
             can be defined at a higher-level now. Of course the new
             <code>
              Object.entries
             </code>
             makes this look silly, but the exercise is still important to the learner.
            </p>
            <p>
             You won't see the full potential of
             <code>
              mapReduce
             </code>
             here, but I share this answer because it's interesting to see just how many places it can be applied. If you're interested in how it is derived and other ways it could be useful, please see
             <a href="https://stackoverflow.com/a/48505969/633183">
              this answer
             </a>
             .
            </p>
           </div>
           <div class="mt24">

         <div class="post-layout">
          <div class="votecell post-layout--left">
           <div class="js-voting-container d-flex jc-center fd-column ai-stretch gs4 fc-black-200" data-post-id="48141962">

          <div class="answercell post-layout--right">
           <div class="s-prose js-post-body" itemprop="text">
            <p>
             I came upon this as a first-item in a Google search trying to learn to do this, and thought I would share for other folsk finding this recently the solution I found, which uses the npm package immutable.
            </p>
            <p>
             I think its interesting to share because immutable uses the OP's EXACT situation in their own documentation - the following is not my own code but pulled from the current immutable-js documentation:
            </p>
            <pre><code>const { Seq } = require('immutable')
const myObject = { a: 1, b: 2, c: 3 }
Seq(myObject).map(x =&gt; x * x).toObject();
// { a: 1, b: 4, c: 9 } 
</code></pre>
            <p>
             Not that Seq has other properties ("Seq describes a lazy operation, allowing them to efficiently chain use of all the higher-order collection methods (such as map and filter) by not creating intermediate collections") and that some other immutable-js data structures might also do the job quite efficiently.
            </p>
            <p>
             Anyone using this method will of course have to
             <code>
              npm install immutable
             </code>
             and might want to read the docs:
            </p>
            <p>
             <a href="https://facebook.github.io/immutable-js/" rel="nofollow noreferrer">
              https://facebook.github.io/immutable-js/
             </a>
            </p>
           </div>

         <div class="post-layout">

          <div class="answercell post-layout--right">
           <div class="s-prose js-post-body" itemprop="text">
            <h2>
             Object Mapper in TypeScript
            </h2>
            <p>
             I like the examples that use
             <code>
              Object.fromEntries
             </code>
             such as
             <a href="https://stackoverflow.com/a/56110762/450913">
              this one
             </a>
             , but still, they are not very easy to use. The answers that use
             <code>
              Object.keys
             </code>
             and then look up the
             <code>
              key
             </code>
             are actually doing multiple look-ups that may not be necessary.
            </p>
            <p>
             I wished there was an
             <code>
              Object.map
             </code>
             function, but we can create our own and call it
             <code>
              objectMap
             </code>
             with the ability to modify both
             <code>
              key
             </code>
             and
             <code>
              value
             </code>
             :
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Usage (JavaScript):
             </strong>
            </p>
            <pre><code>const myObject = { 'a': 1, 'b': 2, 'c': 3 };

// keep the key and modify the value
let obj = objectMap(myObject, val =&gt; val * 2);
// obj = { a: 2, b: 4, c: 6 }


// modify both key and value
obj = objectMap(myObject,
    val =&gt; val * 2 + '',
    key =&gt; (key + key).toUpperCase());
// obj = { AA: '2', BB: '4', CC: '6' }
</code></pre>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Code (TypeScript):
             </strong>
            </p>
            <pre class="lang-js prettyprint-override"><code>interface Dictionary&lt;T&gt; {
    [key: string]: T;
}

function objectMap&lt;TValue, TResult&gt;(
    obj: Dictionary&lt;TValue&gt;,
    valSelector: (val: TValue, obj: Dictionary&lt;TValue&gt;) =&gt; TResult,
    keySelector?: (key: string, obj: Dictionary&lt;TValue&gt;) =&gt; string,
    ctx?: Dictionary&lt;TValue&gt;
) {
    const ret = {} as Dictionary&lt;TResult&gt;;
    for (const key of Object.keys(obj)) {
        const retKey = keySelector
            ? keySelector.call(ctx || null, key, obj)
            : key;
        const retVal = valSelector.call(ctx || null, obj[key], obj);
        ret[retKey] = retVal;
    }
    return ret;
}
</code></pre>
            <p>
             If you are not using TypeScript then copy the above code in
             <a href="http://www.typescriptlang.org/play/" rel="nofollow noreferrer">
              TypeScript Playground
             </a>
             to get the JavaScript code.
            </p>
            <p>
             Also, the reason I put
             <code>
              keySelector
             </code>
             after
             <code>
              valSelector
             </code>
             in the parameter list, is because it is optional.
            </p>
            <p>
             * Some credit go to alexander-mills'
             <a href="https://stackoverflow.com/a/40008272/450913">
              answer
             </a>
             .
            </p>
           </div>
           <div class="mt24">

          <div class="answercell post-layout--right">
           <div class="s-prose js-post-body" itemprop="text">
            <p>
             Based on @Amberlamps answer, here's a utility function
(as a comment it looked ugly)
            </p>
            <pre><code>function mapObject(obj, mapFunc){
    return Object.keys(obj).reduce(function(newObj, value) {
        newObj[value] = mapFunc(obj[value]);
        return newObj;
    }, {});
}
</code></pre>
            <p>
             and the use is:
            </p>
            <pre><code>var obj = {a:1, b:3, c:5}
function double(x){return x * 2}

var newObj = mapObject(obj, double);
//=&gt;  {a: 2, b: 6, c: 10}
</code></pre>
           </div>

        <a name="54563298">
        </a>
        <div class="answer js-answer" data-answerid="54563298" data-highest-scored="0" data-position-on-page="19" data-question-has-accepted-highest-score="1" data-score="2" id="answer-54563298" itemprop="suggestedAnswer" itemscope="" itemtype="https://schema.org/Answer">
         <div class="post-layout">
          <div class="votecell post-layout--left">
           <div class="js-voting-container d-flex jc-center fd-column ai-stretch gs4 fc-black-200" data-post-id="54563298">
            <button aria-label="Up vote" aria-pressed="false" class="js-vote-up-btn flex--item s-btn s-btn__unset c-pointer" data-controller="s-tooltip" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" data-selected-classes="fc-theme-primary" data-unselected-classes="" title="This answer is useful">
             <svg aria-hidden="true" class="svg-icon iconArrowUpLg" height="36" viewbox="0 0 36 36" width="36">
              <path d="M2 25h32L18 9 2 25Z">
              </path>
             </svg>
            </button>
            <div class="js-vote-count flex--item d-flex fd-column ai-center fc-black-500 fs-title" data-value="2" itemprop="upvoteCount">
             2
            </div>
            <button aria-label="Down vote" aria-pressed="false" class="js-vote-down-btn flex--item s-btn s-btn__unset c-pointer" data-controller="s-tooltip" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" data-selected-classes="fc-theme-primary" data-unselected-classes="" title="This answer is not useful">
             <svg aria-hidden="true" class="svg-icon iconArrowDownLg" height="36" viewbox="0 0 36 36" width="36">
              <path d="M2 11h32L18 27 2 11Z">
              </path>
             </svg>
            </button>
            <div aria-label="Accepted" class="js-accepted-answer-indicator flex--item fc-green-500 py6 mtn8 d-none" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" role="note" tabindex="0" title="Loading when this answer was accepted…">
             <div class="ta-center">
              <svg aria-hidden="true" class="svg-icon iconCheckmarkLg" height="36" viewbox="0 0 36 36" width="36">
               <path d="m6 14 8 8L30 6v8L14 30l-8-8v-8Z">
               </path>
              </svg>
             </div>
            </div>
            <a aria-label="Timeline" class="js-post-issue flex--item s-btn s-btn__unset c-pointer py6 mx-auto" data-controller="s-tooltip" data-ks-title="timeline" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" data-shortcut="T" href="/posts/54563298/timeline" title="Show activity on this post.">
             <svg aria-hidden="true" class="mln2 mr0 svg-icon iconHistory" height="18" viewbox="0 0 19 18" width="19">
              <path d="M3 9a8 8 0 1 1 3.73 6.77L8.2 14.3A6 6 0 1 0 5 9l3.01-.01-4 4-4-4h3L3 9Zm7-4h1.01L11 9.36l3.22 2.1-.6.93L10 10V5Z">
              </path>
             </svg>
            </a>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="answercell post-layout--right">
           <div class="s-prose js-post-body" itemprop="text">
            <p>
             My response is largely based off the highest rated response here and hopefully everyone understands (have the same explanation on my GitHub, too). This is why his impementation with map works:
            </p>
            <pre><code>Object.keys(images).map((key) =&gt; images[key] = 'url(' + '"' + images[key] + '"' +    
')');
</code></pre>
            <p>
             The purpose of the function is to take an object and modify the original contents of the object using a method available to all objects (objects and arrays alike) without returning an array. Almost everything within JS is an object, and for that reason elements further down the pipeline of inheritance can potentially technically use those available to those up the line (and the reverse it appears).
            </p>
            <p>
             The reason that this works is due to the .map functions returning an array REQUIRING that you provide an explicit or implicit RETURN of an array instead of simply modifying an existing object. You essentially trick the program into thinking the object is an array by using Object.keys which will allow you to use the map function with its acting on the values the individual keys are associated with (I actually accidentally returned arrays but fixed it). As long as there isn't a return in the normal sense, there will be no array created with the original object stil intact and modified as programmed.
            </p>
            <p>
             This particular program takes an object called images and takes the values of its keys and appends url tags for use within another function. Original is this:
            </p>
            <pre><code>var images = { 
snow: 'https://www.trbimg.com/img-5aa059f5/turbine/bs-md-weather-20180305', 
sunny: 'http://www.cubaweather.org/images/weather-photos/large/Sunny-morning-east-   
Matanzas-city- Cuba-20170131-1080.jpg', 
rain: 'https://i.pinimg.com/originals/23/d8
/ab/23d8ab1eebc72a123cebc80ce32b43d8.jpg' };
</code></pre>
            <p>
             ...and modified is this:
            </p>
            <pre><code>var images = { 
snow: url('https://www.trbimg.com/img-5aa059f5/turbine/bs-md-weather-20180305'),     
sunny: url('http://www.cubaweather.org/images/weather-photos/large/Sunny-morning-   
east-Matanzas-city- Cuba-20170131-1080.jpg'), 
rain: url('https://i.pinimg.com/originals/23/d8
/ab/23d8ab1eebc72a123cebc80ce32b43d8.jpg') 
};
</code></pre>
            <p>
             The object's original structure is left intact allowing for normal property access as long as there isn't a return. Do NOT have it return an array like normal and everything will be fine. The goal is REASSIGNING the original values (images[key]) to what is wanted and not anything else. As far as I know, in order to prevent array output there HAS to be REASSIGNMENT of images[key] and no implicit or explicit request to return an array (variable assignment does this and was glitching back and forth for me).
            </p>
            <p>
             EDIT:
            </p>
            <p>
             Going to address his other method regarding new object creation to avoid modifying original object (and reassignment appears to still be necessary in order to avoid accidentally creating an array as output). These functions use arrow syntax and are if you simply want to create a new object for future use.
            </p>
            <pre><code>const mapper = (obj, mapFn) =&gt; Object.keys(obj).reduce((result, key) =&gt; {
                result[key] = mapFn(obj)[key];
                return result;
            }, {});

var newImages = mapper(images, (value) =&gt; value);
</code></pre>
            <p>
             The way these functions work is like so:
            </p>
            <p>
             mapFn takes the function to be added later (in this case (value) =&gt; value) and simply returns whatever is stored there as a value for that key (or multiplied by two if you change the return value like he did) in mapFn(obj)[key],
            </p>
            <p>
             and then redefines the original value associated with the key in result[key] = mapFn(obj)[key]
            </p>
            <p>
             and returns the operation performed on result (the accumulator located in the brackets initiated at the end of the .reduce function).
            </p>
            <p>
             All of this is being performed on the chosen object and STILL there CANNOT be an implicit request for a returned array and only works when reassigning values as far as I can tell. This requires some mental gymnastics but reduces the lines of code needed as can be seen above. Output is exactly the same as can be seen below:
            </p>
            <pre><code>{snow: "https://www.trbimg.com/img-5aa059f5/turbine/bs-   
md-weather-20180305", sunny: "http://www.cubaweather.org/images/weather-
photos/l…morning-east-Matanzas-city-Cuba-20170131-1080.jpg", rain: 
"https://i.pinimg.com/originals/23/d8
/ab/23d8ab1eebc72a123cebc80ce32b43d8.jpg"}
</code></pre>
            <p>
             Keep in mind this worked with NON-NUMBERS. You CAN duplicate ANY object by SIMPLY RETURNING THE VALUE in the mapFN function.
            </p>
           </div>
           <div class="mt24">
            <div class="d-flex fw-wrap ai-start jc-end gs8 gsy">

        <div class="answer js-answer" data-answerid="58458409" data-highest-scored="0" data-position-on-page="20" data-question-has-accepted-highest-score="1" data-score="2" id="answer-58458409" itemprop="suggestedAnswer" itemscope="" itemtype="https://schema.org/Answer">
         <div class="post-layout">
          <div class="votecell post-layout--left">
           <div class="js-voting-container d-flex jc-center fd-column ai-stretch gs4 fc-black-200" data-post-id="58458409">
            <button aria-label="Up vote" aria-pressed="false" class="js-vote-up-btn flex--item s-btn s-btn__unset c-pointer" data-controller="s-tooltip" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" data-selected-classes="fc-theme-primary" data-unselected-classes="" title="This answer is useful">
             <svg aria-hidden="true" class="svg-icon iconArrowUpLg" height="36" viewbox="0 0 36 36" width="36">
              <path d="M2 25h32L18 9 2 25Z">
              </path>
             </svg>
            </button>
            <div class="js-vote-count flex--item d-flex fd-column ai-center fc-black-500 fs-title" data-value="2" itemprop="upvoteCount">
             2
            </div>
            <button aria-label="Down vote" aria-pressed="false" class="js-vote-down-btn flex--item s-btn s-btn__unset c-pointer" data-controller="s-tooltip" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" data-selected-classes="fc-theme-primary" data-unselected-classes="" title="This answer is not useful">
             <svg aria-hidden="true" class="svg-icon iconArrowDownLg" height="36" viewbox="0 0 36 36" width="36">
              <path d="M2 11h32L18 27 2 11Z">
              </path>
             </svg>
            </button>
            <div aria-label="Accepted" class="js-accepted-answer-indicator flex--item fc-green-500 py6 mtn8 d-none" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" role="note" tabindex="0" title="Loading when this answer was accepted…">
             <div class="ta-center">
              <svg aria-hidden="true" class="svg-icon iconCheckmarkLg" height="36" viewbox="0 0 36 36" width="36">
               <path d="m6 14 8 8L30 6v8L14 30l-8-8v-8Z">
               </path>
              </svg>
             </div>
            </div>
            <a aria-label="Timeline" class="js-post-issue flex--item s-btn s-btn__unset c-pointer py6 mx-auto" data-controller="s-tooltip" data-ks-title="timeline" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" data-shortcut="T" href="/posts/58458409/timeline" title="Show activity on this post.">
             <svg aria-hidden="true" class="mln2 mr0 svg-icon iconHistory" height="18" viewbox="0 0 19 18" width="19">
              <path d="M3 9a8 8 0 1 1 3.73 6.77L8.2 14.3A6 6 0 1 0 5 9l3.01-.01-4 4-4-4h3L3 9Zm7-4h1.01L11 9.36l3.22 2.1-.6.93L10 10V5Z">
              </path>
             </svg>
            </a>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="answercell post-layout--right">
           <div class="s-prose js-post-body" itemprop="text">
            <pre><code>const mapObject = (targetObject, callbackFn) =&gt; {
    if (!targetObject) return targetObject;
    if (Array.isArray(targetObject)){
        return targetObject.map((v)=&gt;mapObject(v, callbackFn))
    }
    return Object.entries(targetObject).reduce((acc,[key, value]) =&gt; {
        const res = callbackFn(key, value);
        if (!Array.isArray(res) &amp;&amp; typeof res ==='object'){
            return {...acc, [key]: mapObject(res, callbackFn)}
        }
        if (Array.isArray(res)){
            return {...acc, [key]: res.map((v)=&gt;mapObject(v, callbackFn))}
        }
        return {...acc, [key]: res};
    },{})
};
const mapped = mapObject(a,(key,value)=&gt; {
    if (!Array.isArray(value) &amp;&amp; key === 'a') return ;
    if (!Array.isArray(value) &amp;&amp; key === 'e') return [];
    if (!Array.isArray(value) &amp;&amp; key === 'g') return value * value;
    return value;
});
console.log(JSON.stringify(mapped)); 
// {"b":2,"c":[{"d":2,"e":[],"f":[{"g":4}]}]}
</code></pre>
            <p>
             This function goes recursively through the object and arrays of objects. Attributes can be deleted if returned undefined
            </p>
           </div>

        <div class="answer js-answer" data-answerid="29078153" data-highest-scored="0" data-position-on-page="21" data-question-has-accepted-highest-score="1" data-score="1" id="answer-29078153" itemprop="suggestedAnswer" itemscope="" itemtype="https://schema.org/Answer">
         <div class="post-layout">
          <div class="votecell post-layout--left">
           <div class="js-voting-container d-flex jc-center fd-column ai-stretch gs4 fc-black-200" data-post-id="29078153">
            <button aria-label="Up vote" aria-pressed="false" class="js-vote-up-btn flex--item s-btn s-btn__unset c-pointer" data-controller="s-tooltip" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" data-selected-classes="fc-theme-primary" data-unselected-classes="" title="This answer is useful">

            </div>
            <button aria-label="Down vote" aria-pressed="false" class="js-vote-down-btn flex--item s-btn s-btn__unset c-pointer" data-controller="s-tooltip" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" data-selected-classes="fc-theme-primary" data-unselected-classes="" title="This answer is not useful">

              </path>

            <div aria-label="Accepted" class="js-accepted-answer-indicator flex--item fc-green-500 py6 mtn8 d-none" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" role="note" tabindex="0" title="Loading when this answer was accepted…">
             <div class="ta-center">
              <svg aria-hidden="true" class="svg-icon iconCheckmarkLg" height="36" viewbox="0 0 36 36" width="36">

            <a aria-label="Timeline" class="js-post-issue flex--item s-btn s-btn__unset c-pointer py6 mx-auto" data-controller="s-tooltip" data-ks-title="timeline" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" data-shortcut="T" href="/posts/29078153/timeline" title="Show activity on this post.">
             <svg aria-hidden="true" class="mln2 mr0 svg-icon iconHistory" height="18" viewbox="0 0 19 18" width="19">
              <path d="M3 9a8 8 0 1 1 3.73 6.77L8.2 14.3A6 6 0 1 0 5 9l3.01-.01-4 4-4-4h3L3 9Zm7-4h1.01L11 9.36l3.22 2.1-.6.93L10 10V5Z">

             </svg>
            </a>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="answercell post-layout--right">
           <div class="s-prose js-post-body" itemprop="text">
            <p>
             If you're interested in
             <code>
              map
             </code>
             ping not only values but also keys, I have written
             <a href="https://github.com/MattiSG/Object.map.js/blob/master/README.md" rel="nofollow">
              <code>
               Object.map(valueMapper, keyMapper)
              </code>
             </a>
             , that behaves this way:
            </p>
            <pre><code>var source = { a: 1, b: 2 };
function sum(x) { return x + x }

source.map(sum);            // returns { a: 2, b: 4 }
source.map(undefined, sum); // returns { aa: 1, bb: 2 }
source.map(sum, sum);       // returns { aa: 2, bb: 4 }
</code></pre>
           </div>

        <div class="answer js-answer" data-answerid="38887313" data-highest-scored="0" data-position-on-page="22" data-question-has-accepted-highest-score="1" data-score="1" id="answer-38887313" itemprop="suggestedAnswer" itemscope="" itemtype="https://schema.org/Answer">
         <div class="post-layout">
          <div class="votecell post-layout--left">
           <div class="js-voting-container d-flex jc-center fd-column ai-stretch gs4 fc-black-200" data-post-id="38887313">

          <div class="answercell post-layout--right">
           <div class="s-prose js-post-body" itemprop="text">
            <p>
             I needed a version that allowed modifying the keys as well (based on @Amberlamps and @yonatanmn answers);
            </p>
            <pre><code>var facts = [ // can be an object or array - see jsfiddle below
    {uuid:"asdfasdf",color:"red"},
    {uuid:"sdfgsdfg",color:"green"},
    {uuid:"dfghdfgh",color:"blue"}
];

var factObject = mapObject({}, facts, function(key, item) {
    return [item.uuid, {test:item.color, oldKey:key}];
});

function mapObject(empty, obj, mapFunc){
    return Object.keys(obj).reduce(function(newObj, key) {
        var kvPair = mapFunc(key, obj[key]);
        newObj[kvPair[0]] = kvPair[1];
        return newObj;
    }, empty);
}
</code></pre>
            <p>
             factObject=
            </p>
            <pre><code>{
"asdfasdf": {"color":"red","oldKey":"0"},
"sdfgsdfg": {"color":"green","oldKey":"1"},
"dfghdfgh": {"color":"blue","oldKey":"2"}
}
</code></pre>
            <p>
             Edit: slight change to pass in the starting object {}.  Allows it to be [] (if the keys are integers)
            </p>
           </div>

           <div class="s-prose js-post-body" itemprop="text">
            <pre><code>var myObject = { 'a': 1, 'b': 2, 'c': 3 };


Object.prototype.map = function(fn){
    var oReturn = {};
    for (sCurObjectPropertyName in this) {
        oReturn[sCurObjectPropertyName] = fn(this[sCurObjectPropertyName], sCurObjectPropertyName);
    }
    return oReturn;
}
Object.defineProperty(Object.prototype,'map',{enumerable:false});





newObject = myObject.map(function (value, label) {
    return value * value;
});


// newObject is now { 'a': 1, 'b': 4, 'c': 9 }
</code></pre>

        <a name="53692416">
        </a>
        <div class="answer js-answer" data-answerid="53692416" data-highest-scored="0" data-position-on-page="24" data-question-has-accepted-highest-score="1" data-score="1" id="answer-53692416" itemprop="suggestedAnswer" itemscope="" itemtype="https://schema.org/Answer">
         <div class="post-layout">
          <div class="votecell post-layout--left">
           <div class="js-voting-container d-flex jc-center fd-column ai-stretch gs4 fc-black-200" data-post-id="53692416">
            <button aria-label="Up vote" aria-pressed="false" class="js-vote-up-btn flex--item s-btn s-btn__unset c-pointer" data-controller="s-tooltip" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" data-selected-classes="fc-theme-primary" data-unselected-classes="" title="This answer is useful">
             <svg aria-hidden="true" class="svg-icon iconArrowUpLg" height="36" viewbox="0 0 36 36" width="36">
              <path d="M2 25h32L18 9 2 25Z">
              </path>
             </svg>
            </button>
            <div class="js-vote-count flex--item d-flex fd-column ai-center fc-black-500 fs-title" data-value="1" itemprop="upvoteCount">
             1
            </div>
            <button aria-label="Down vote" aria-pressed="false" class="js-vote-down-btn flex--item s-btn s-btn__unset c-pointer" data-controller="s-tooltip" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" data-selected-classes="fc-theme-primary" data-unselected-classes="" title="This answer is not useful">
             <svg aria-hidden="true" class="svg-icon iconArrowDownLg" height="36" viewbox="0 0 36 36" width="36">
              <path d="M2 11h32L18 27 2 11Z">
              </path>
             </svg>
            </button>
            <div aria-label="Accepted" class="js-accepted-answer-indicator flex--item fc-green-500 py6 mtn8 d-none" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" role="note" tabindex="0" title="Loading when this answer was accepted…">
             <div class="ta-center">
              <svg aria-hidden="true" class="svg-icon iconCheckmarkLg" height="36" viewbox="0 0 36 36" width="36">
               <path d="m6 14 8 8L30 6v8L14 30l-8-8v-8Z">
               </path>
              </svg>
             </div>
            </div>
            <a aria-label="Timeline" class="js-post-issue flex--item s-btn s-btn__unset c-pointer py6 mx-auto" data-controller="s-tooltip" data-ks-title="timeline" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" data-shortcut="T" href="/posts/53692416/timeline" title="Show activity on this post.">
             <svg aria-hidden="true" class="mln2 mr0 svg-icon iconHistory" height="18" viewbox="0 0 19 18" width="19">
              <path d="M3 9a8 8 0 1 1 3.73 6.77L8.2 14.3A6 6 0 1 0 5 9l3.01-.01-4 4-4-4h3L3 9Zm7-4h1.01L11 9.36l3.22 2.1-.6.93L10 10V5Z">
              </path>
             </svg>
            </a>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="answercell post-layout--right">
           <div class="s-prose js-post-body" itemprop="text">
            <p>
             To responds more closely to what
             <em>
              precisely
             </em>
             the OP asked for, the OP wants an object:
            </p>
            <blockquote>
             <p>
              <code>
               myObject = { 'a': 1, 'b': 2, 'c': 3 }
              </code>
             </p>
            </blockquote>
            <p>
             to have a map method
             <code>
              myObject.map
             </code>
             ,
            </p>
            <blockquote>
             <p>
              similar to Array.prototype.map that would be used as follows:
             </p>
             <pre>newObject = myObject.map(function (value, label) {
    return value * value;
});
// newObject is now { 'a': 1, 'b': 4, 'c': 9 }</pre>
            </blockquote>
            <p>
             The
             <em>
              imho
             </em>
             best (measured in terms to "
             <em>
              close to what is asked
             </em>
             " + "no ES{5,6,7} required needlessly") answer would be:
            </p>
            <pre><code>myObject.map = function mapForObject(callback)
{
  var result = {};
  for(var property in this){
    if(this.hasOwnProperty(property) &amp;&amp; property != "map"){
      result[property] = callback(this[property],property,this);
    }
  }
  return result;
}
</code></pre>
            <p>
             The code above avoids intentionally using any language features, only available in recent ECMAScript editions. With the code above the problem can be solved lke this:
            </p>
            <p>
             <div class="snippet" data-babel="false" data-console="false" data-hide="false" data-lang="js">
              <div class="snippet-code">
               <pre class="snippet-code-js lang-js prettyprint-override"><code>myObject = { 'a': 1, 'b': 2, 'c': 3 };

myObject.map = function mapForObject(callback)
{
  var result = {};
  for(var property in this){
    if(this.hasOwnProperty(property) &amp;&amp; property != "map"){
      result[property] = callback(this[property],property,this);
    }
  }
  return result;
}

newObject = myObject.map(function (value, label) {
  return value * value;
});
console.log("newObject is now",newObject);</code></pre>
              </div>
             </div>
             <a href="https://alexmahr.de/runjavascript.html#bXlPYmplY3QgPSB7ICdhJzogMSwgJ2InOiAyLCAnYyc6IDMgfTsKCm15T2JqZWN0Lm1hcCA9IGZ1bmN0aW9uIG1hcEZvck9iamVjdChjYWxsYmFjaykKewogIHZhciByZXN1bHQgPSB7fTsKICBmb3IodmFyIHByb3BlcnR5IGluIHRoaXMpewogICAgaWYodGhpcy5oYXNPd25Qcm9wZXJ0eShwcm9wZXJ0eSkgJiYgcHJvcGVydHkgIT0gIm1hcCIpewogICAgICByZXN1bHRbcHJvcGVydHldID0gY2FsbGJhY2sodGhpc1twcm9wZXJ0eV0scHJvcGVydHksdGhpcyk7CiAgICB9CiAgfQogIHJldHVybiByZXN1bHQ7Cn0KCm5ld09iamVjdCA9IG15T2JqZWN0Lm1hcChmdW5jdGlvbiAodmFsdWUsIGxhYmVsKSB7CiAgcmV0dXJuIHZhbHVlICogdmFsdWU7Cn0pOwpjb25zb2xlLmxvZygibmV3T2JqZWN0IGlzIG5vdyIsbmV3T2JqZWN0KTs=" rel="nofollow noreferrer">
              alternative test code here
             </a>
            </p>
            <p>
             Besides frowned upon by some, it would be a possibility to insert the solution in the prototype chain like this.
            </p>
            <pre><code>Object.prototype.map = function(callback)
{
  var result = {};
  for(var property in this){
    if(this.hasOwnProperty(property)){
      result[property] = callback(this[property],property,this);
    }
  }
  return result;
}
</code></pre>
            <p>
             Something, which when done with careful oversight should not have any ill effects and not impact
             <code>
              map
             </code>
             method of other objects (i.e. Array's
             <code>
              map
             </code>
             ).
            </p>
           </div>
           <div class="mt24">
            <div class="d-flex fw-wrap ai-start jc-end gs8 gsy">
             <time datetime="2018-12-09T12:44:33" itemprop="dateCreated">
             </time>

         <div class="post-layout">
          <div class="votecell post-layout--left">
           <div class="js-voting-container d-flex jc-center fd-column ai-stretch gs4 fc-black-200" data-post-id="54118770">
            <button aria-label="Up vote" aria-pressed="false" class="js-vote-up-btn flex--item s-btn s-btn__unset c-pointer" data-controller="s-tooltip" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" data-selected-classes="fc-theme-primary" data-unselected-classes="" title="This answer is useful">

            <a aria-label="Timeline" class="js-post-issue flex--item s-btn s-btn__unset c-pointer py6 mx-auto" data-controller="s-tooltip" data-ks-title="timeline" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" data-shortcut="T" href="/posts/54118770/timeline" title="Show activity on this post.">

          <div class="answercell post-layout--right">
           <div class="s-prose js-post-body" itemprop="text">
            <p>
             First, convert your HTMLCollection using Object.entries(collection). Then it’s an iterable you can now use the .map method on it.
            </p>
            <pre><code>Object.entries(collection).map(...)
</code></pre>
            <p>
             reference
             <a href="https://medium.com/@js_tut/calling-javascript-code-on-multiple-div-elements-without-the-id-attribute-97ff6a50f31" rel="nofollow noreferrer">
              https://medium.com/@js_tut/calling-javascript-code-on-multiple-div-elements-without-the-id-attribute-97ff6a50f31
             </a>
            </p>
           </div>

         <div class="post-layout">
          <div class="votecell post-layout--left">

          <div class="answercell post-layout--right">
           <div class="s-prose js-post-body" itemprop="text">
            <p>
             I handle only strings to reduce exemptions:
            </p>
            <pre><code>Object.keys(params).map(k =&gt; typeof params[k] == "string" ? params[k] = params[k].trim() : null);
</code></pre>

          <div class="answercell post-layout--right">
           <div class="s-prose js-post-body" itemprop="text">
            <p>
             Hey wrote a little mapper function that might help.
            </p>
            <pre><code>    function propertyMapper(object, src){
         for (var property in object) {   
           for (var sourceProp in src) {
               if(property === sourceProp){
                 if(Object.prototype.toString.call( property ) === '[object Array]'){
                   propertyMapper(object[property], src[sourceProp]);
                   }else{
                   object[property] = src[sourceProp];
                }
              }
            }
         }
      }
</code></pre>
           </div>

         <div class="post-layout">

           <div class="js-voting-container d-flex jc-center fd-column ai-stretch gs4 fc-black-200" data-post-id="50477897">

          <div class="answercell post-layout--right">
           <div class="s-prose js-post-body" itemprop="text">
            <p>
             If anyone was looking for a simple solution that maps an object to a new object or to an array:
            </p>
            <pre><code>// Maps an object to a new object by applying a function to each key+value pair.
// Takes the object to map and a function from (key, value) to mapped value.
const mapObject = (obj, fn) =&gt; {
    const newObj = {};
    Object.keys(obj).forEach(k =&gt; { newObj[k] = fn(k, obj[k]); });
    return newObj;
};

// Maps an object to a new array by applying a function to each key+value pair.
// Takes the object to map and a function from (key, value) to mapped value.
const mapObjectToArray = (obj, fn) =&gt; (
    Object.keys(obj).map(k =&gt; fn(k, obj[k]))
);
</code></pre>
            <p>
             This may not work for all objects or all mapping functions, but it works for plain shallow objects and straightforward mapping functions which is all I needed.
            </p>
           </div>

          <div class="answercell post-layout--right">
           <div class="s-prose js-post-body" itemprop="text">
            <p>
             A different take on it is to use a custom json stringify function that can also work on deep objects. This might be useful if you intend to post it to the server anyway as json
            </p>
            <p>
             <div class="snippet" data-babel="false" data-console="true" data-hide="false" data-lang="js">
              <div class="snippet-code">
               <pre class="snippet-code-js lang-js prettyprint-override"><code>const obj = { 'a': 1, 'b': 2, x: {'c': 3 }}
const json = JSON.stringify(obj, (k, v) =&gt; typeof v === 'number' ? v * v : v)

console.log(json)
console.log('back to json:', JSON.parse(json))</code></pre>
              </div>
             </div>
            </p>
           </div>

        <div class="answer js-answer" data-answerid="67572624" data-highest-scored="0" data-position-on-page="30" data-question-has-accepted-highest-score="1" data-score="0" id="answer-67572624" itemprop="suggestedAnswer" itemscope="" itemtype="https://schema.org/Answer">
         <div class="post-layout">
          <div class="votecell post-layout--left">
           <div class="js-voting-container d-flex jc-center fd-column ai-stretch gs4 fc-black-200" data-post-id="67572624">
            <button aria-label="Up vote" aria-pressed="false" class="js-vote-up-btn flex--item s-btn s-btn__unset c-pointer" data-controller="s-tooltip" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" data-selected-classes="fc-theme-primary" data-unselected-classes="" title="This answer is useful">
             <svg aria-hidden="true" class="svg-icon iconArrowUpLg" height="36" viewbox="0 0 36 36" width="36">
              <path d="M2 25h32L18 9 2 25Z">
              </path>
             </svg>
            </button>
            <div class="js-vote-count flex--item d-flex fd-column ai-center fc-black-500 fs-title" data-value="0" itemprop="upvoteCount">
             0
            </div>
            <button aria-label="Down vote" aria-pressed="false" class="js-vote-down-btn flex--item s-btn s-btn__unset c-pointer" data-controller="s-tooltip" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" data-selected-classes="fc-theme-primary" data-unselected-classes="" title="This answer is not useful">
             <svg aria-hidden="true" class="svg-icon iconArrowDownLg" height="36" viewbox="0 0 36 36" width="36">
              <path d="M2 11h32L18 27 2 11Z">
              </path>
             </svg>
            </button>
            <div aria-label="Accepted" class="js-accepted-answer-indicator flex--item fc-green-500 py6 mtn8 d-none" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" role="note" tabindex="0" title="Loading when this answer was accepted…">
             <div class="ta-center">
              <svg aria-hidden="true" class="svg-icon iconCheckmarkLg" height="36" viewbox="0 0 36 36" width="36">
               <path d="m6 14 8 8L30 6v8L14 30l-8-8v-8Z">
               </path>
              </svg>
             </div>
            </div>
            <a aria-label="Timeline" class="js-post-issue flex--item s-btn s-btn__unset c-pointer py6 mx-auto" data-controller="s-tooltip" data-ks-title="timeline" data-s-tooltip-placement="right" data-shortcut="T" href="/posts/67572624/timeline" title="Show activity on this post.">
             <svg aria-hidden="true" class="mln2 mr0 svg-icon iconHistory" height="18" viewbox="0 0 19 18" width="19">
              <path d="M3 9a8 8 0 1 1 3.73 6.77L8.2 14.3A6 6 0 1 0 5 9l3.01-.01-4 4-4-4h3L3 9Zm7-4h1.01L11 9.36l3.22 2.1-.6.93L10 10V5Z">
              </path>
             </svg>
            </a>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="answercell post-layout--right">
           <div class="s-prose js-post-body" itemprop="text">
            <p>
             I needed a function to optionally map not only (nor exclusively) values, but also keys. The original object should not change. The object contained only primitive values also.
            </p>
            <pre><code>function mappedObject(obj, keyMapper, valueMapper) {

    const mapped = {};
    const keys   = Object.keys(obj);
    const mapKey = typeof keyMapper == 'function';
    const mapVal = typeof valueMapper == 'function';

    for (let i = 0; i &lt; keys.length; i++) {
        const key = mapKey ? keyMapper(keys[i]) : keys[i];
        const val = mapVal ? valueMapper(obj[keys[i]]) : obj[keys[i]];
        mapped[key] = val;
    }

    return mapped;
}
</code></pre>
            <p>
             Use. Pass a keymapper and a valuemapper function:
            </p>
            <pre><code>const o1 = { x: 1, c: 2 }
mappedObject(o1, k =&gt; k + '0', v =&gt; v + 1) // {x0: 2, c0: 3}
</code></pre>
           </div>
